Talaq — Divorce

Mourning (Ihdad) for Widows and Permanently Divorced Women
States the ruling on mourning for women after final divorce or husband's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mourning (ihdad) for widows and permanently divorced women, explain the key difference with the Shafi'i school, and apply the Hanafi proofs (dalil) and qiyas to defend the position.

Core Idea
The loss of the marriage bond obligates mourning, whether by death or final divorce — both are a loss of protection and sufficiency.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on mourning (ihdad) for women after the death of a husband or after a final, irrevocable divorce. The text from al-Hidayah and al-Quduri establishes that both categories must observe ihdad. We will explore the primary evidence from hadith, the school's qiyas extending the ruling to divorced women, and the Shafi'i objection. Understanding this ruling illuminates how the Hanafi school applies textual proofs and analogical reasoning to derive consistent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories and the ruling
Read the opening of the fasl: ihdad is wajib upon the mutabbatah (permanently divorced) and the widow, provided she is a mature Muslim. Note the ruling is wajib, not fard.
The condition of being a mature Muslim is common to both categories.
2
Examine the proof for widows
The primary proof is the hadith: 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to mourn for a dead person more than three days, except for her husband, four months and ten days.' This establishes ihdad for widows directly.
The exception 'except for her husband' is key; it shows the ruling is specific to the husband's death.
3
Extend the ruling to the mutabbatah via qiyas
The Hanafi school uses qiyas: both the widow and the permanently divorced woman have lost the marriage bond, which is a blessing of protection and sufficiency. The text argues that separation is even more abrupt than death, so mourning is even more appropriate.
The loss of the marriage itself is the illa (effective cause) for ihdad, regardless of how it ended.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Al-Shafi'i argues that ihdad is regret for the loss of a husband, but a divorced woman has been estranged and should not regret his loss. The Hanafi response: regret is for the loss of the marriage bond itself, which is a blessing. Furthermore, the hadith forbidding henna for a woman in 'iddah applies to both widows and divorced women.
The hadith about henna is used as an additional proof that any woman in 'iddah must avoid beautification.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to the Hanafi school, a divorced woman must avoid perfume, dyes, and beautification during her 'iddah. According to al-Shafi'i, she may adorn herself. This difference affects daily practice in Muslim communities.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school is that ihdad is wajib for both categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل قال وعلى المبتوتة والمتوفى عنها زوجها اذا كانت بالغة مسلمة الحداد اما المتوفى عنها زوجها فلقوله عليه السلام لا يحل لامرأة تومن بالله واليوم الأخران تحد على ميت فوق ثلثة ايام الاعلى زوجها اربعة اشهر و عشرا واما المبتوتة فمذهبنا وقال الشافعى لاحداد عليها لانه وجب اظهار اللتاسف على فوت زوج وفى. بعهدها الى مماته وقد او حشها بالابانة فلاتاسف بفوته ولناماروى ان النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى المعتدة ان تختضب بالحناء وقال الحناء طيب ولانه يجب اظهارا للتاسف على فوت نعمة النكاح الذى هو سبب لصونها وكفاية منها والابانة اقطع لها من الموت حتى كان لها ان تغسله ميتا قبل الابانة لابعدها

ترجمه قدوری نے کہا جس عورت کی اپنے شوہر سے قطعی جدائی ہوئی (خواہ بیک طلاق یا بہ طلاق یا خلع ) اور جس عورت کو چھوڑ کر اس کا شوہر مر گیا تو اس پر سوگ رکھنا واجب ہے جب وہ مسلمان بالغہ ہو ۔ بہر حال متوفی عنہاز وجھا تو اس لئے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے کہ
Fasl: He said: Upon the woman with a permanent separation (mutabbatah) and the woman whose husband dies, if she is a mature Muslim, mourning (ihdad) is obligatory. As for the one whose husband dies, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to mourn for a dead person more than three days, except for her husband, four months and ten days.' As for the permanently separated woman, it is our madhhab, and al-Shafi'i said: She is not required to mourn because mourning is to display regret for the loss of a husband, but he has already estranged her by separation, so she does not regret his loss. And we have the narration that the Prophet, peace be upon him, forbade the woman in 'iddah from dyeing with henna and said: 'Henna is perfume.' And because it is necessary to display regret for the loss of the blessing of marriage, which is a means of protection and sufficiency. And separation is more abrupt than death, so she is allowed to wash him after death before separation, not after.

Translation: Quduri said: A woman who has been permanently separated from her husband (whether by one irrevocable divorce, three divorces, or khul') and a woman whose husband has died, must observe mourning (soog) if she is a mature Muslim. As for the widow, it is because of the Prophet's saying, peace be upon him: ...
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This is a new section (fasl) beginning a ruling on mourning (ihdad). The text is split between Arabic matn and Urdu commentary. The ruling: Both a permanently divorced woman (mutabbatah) and a widow must observe ihdad if she is a mature Muslim. The proof for the widow is the famous hadith that a woman may not mourn beyond three days except for her husband for four months and ten days. For the permanently divorced woman, the Hanafi school holds that ihdad is obligatory, while Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that mourning is to express sorrow over the loss of a husband, but the divorced woman has already been separated and should not feel sorrow. The Hanafi proof: The Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) forbade a woman in 'iddah from using henna and called it perfume, indicating that she must avoid beautification, which is part of mourning. Additionally, mourning is for the loss of the blessing of marriage, which is a means of protection and sufficiency; the divorced woman also loses that blessing. The text also notes that separation (separation by divorce) is even more abrupt than death, so it requires mourning.

Key Terms
حداد (ihdad): Mourning: abstention from adornment, perfume, and beautification for a prescribed period after divorce or death.
مبتوتة (mutabbatah): A woman who has been permanently separated from her husband by an irrevocable divorce (ba'in) or khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence used by the Hanafi school to require mourning (ihdad) for a permanently divorced woman?
A) The Quranic verse on 'iddah.
B) Analogy from the mourning of a widow, as both lose the marriage bond.
C) A direct hadith about divorced women.
D) Consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, mourning (ihdad) is wajib for both widows and permanently divorced women because both have lost the blessing of marriage, which is a means of protection and sufficiency.

No 'Iddah for Harbi Women Who Embrace Islam
Explains the ruling on 'iddah for harbi women using Quran and rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the 'iddah of a harbi woman who converts to Islam and explain the scriptural and rational proofs, including the exception for pregnancy.

Core Idea
A harbi woman does not observe 'iddah because her husband's lineage is not protected by Islamic law.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a woman from dar al-harb embraces Islam and emigrates to Muslims. What is her 'iddah obligation? The author presents both a Quranic proof (Surah al-Mumtahanah) and a rational argument (dalil aqli) to show that no 'iddah is required. The lesson also covers an important exception for pregnant women and an intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is marrying an emigrant harbi woman who has converted to Islam. The ruling is that she does not need to observe any 'iddah; the marriage is permissible immediately unless she is pregnant.
The absence of 'iddah is the default, based on the absolute permission in the Quran.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites the Quranic verse (Surah al-Mumtahanah 60:10) which gives absolute permission to marry the emigrant women. No condition of 'iddah is mentioned. The rational proof is also given: 'iddah is to protect the husband's lineage.
The proof is both naqli (Quran) and aqli (rational).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
The verse says 'There is no sin upon you that you marry them' without any qualification. Adding an 'iddah condition would be an addition to the text. The rational proof links 'iddah to lineage protection; a harbi's lineage is not honorable (like an animal), so protection is unnecessary.
The wajh al-dalalah hinges on the generality of the permission and the purpose of 'iddah.
4
Note the exception for pregnancy
If the harbi woman is pregnant, marriage is not permissible until delivery. This is because the child's lineage is established (through the bed, firash), and marrying her would create two simultaneous beds, which is prohibited.
The exception shows that lineage protection is still relevant when lineage is established.
5
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifah has a narration allowing marriage to a pregnant harbi convert while prohibiting intercourse, likening it to a pregnant adulteress. However, the author rejects this analogy because the child of a harbi has established lineage, unlike zina. The preferred view is impermissibility of marriage until delivery.
The tarjih is based on the difference in lineage establishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العدد (بيان القرآن) اس آیت سے استدلال اس طرح پر ہوگا اللہ نے مہاجرہ عورتوں کے ساتھ نکاح کرنے کی مطلقاً اجازت دی ہے چنا نچہ فر مایا لا جناح عليكم ان تنكحوهن پس اگر اس نکاح کی اجازت کو عدت گذرنے کی بعد کے ساتھ مقید کیا گیا تو نص قرآنی پر زیادتی کرنا لازم آئے گا جو صحیح نہیں ہے اور دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ عدت جہاں بھی ہو گی اس میں آدمی کا حق ہوتا ہے کیونکہ عورت پر عدت شوہر کے پانی کی حفاظت کے لئے واجب ہوتی ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ طلاق قبل الدخول کی صورت میں عورت پر عدت واجب نہیں ہوتی اور حربی کا فر پتھروں اور بہائم کے مشابہ ہے حتی کہ اس پر رقیت ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اور اس کو بازار میں جانور کی طرح فروخت کیا جاتا ہے پس جب 7 بی جہاد کے ساتھ ملحق ہے تو اس کا پانی قابل احترام نہیں لہذا اس کی حفاظت بھی نہیں کی جائے گی اور جب اس کے پانی کی حفاظت واجب نہیں تو اس کی بیوی پر عدت بھی واجب نہیں ہوگی ۔ ہاں اگر جر بی کی بیوی حاملہ ہو تو وضع حمل سے پہلے اس کے ساتھ نکاح کرنا جائز نہیں کیونکہ اس کے پیٹ میں جو بچہ وہ ثابت النسب ہے اور فراش موجود ہے اب اگر اس کو نکاح کی اجازت دیدی جائے تو جمع بین الفراشین لازم آئے گا حالانکہ شرعا جمع بین الفراشین ممنوع ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ بھی ہے کہ مہاجرہ حاملہ کے ساتھ نکاح جائز ہے البتہ ولی کرنا جائز نہیں، جیسا کہ حاملہ من الزنا کے ساتھ نکاح صحیح ہے مگر وطی کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے اور قول اول یعنی عدم جواز نکاح کا قول زیادہ صحیح ہے کیونکہ حمل من الزنا کا نسب ثابت نہیں ہے اور یہاں حربی سے نسب ثابت ہے لہذا اس کو حاملہ من الزنا پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
The number (explanation of the Quran) - The deduction from this verse will be as follows: Allah has absolutely permitted marrying the emigrant women, as He said: 'There is no sin upon you that you marry them.' So if this permission to marry is restricted to after the passage of the 'iddah, then it would necessitate adding to the Quranic text, which is not correct. And the rational proof is that wherever 'iddah is required, there is a right of the man, because 'iddah is obligatory upon a woman to protect the husband's lineage. That is why in the case of divorce before consummation, 'iddah is not obligatory. And a harbi disbeliever resembles stones and beasts, to the extent that slavery is established upon him and he is sold in the market like an animal. So when he is attached to war, his lineage is not honorable, therefore his lineage will not be protected, and when protection of his lineage is not obligatory, then 'iddah upon his wife is not obligatory. Yes, if the harbi's wife is pregnant, it is not permissible to marry her before delivery, because the child in her womb has established lineage and the bed exists. Now if permission to marry her is given, then it would require having two beds simultaneously, while Shari'ah prohibits having two beds. There is also a narration from Imam Abu Hanifah that marrying a pregnant emigrant woman is permissible, but intercourse is not permissible, just as marrying a pregnant woman from zina is valid but intercourse is not valid. And the first statement (i.e., the impermissibility of marriage) is more correct, because the lineage of a child from zina is not established, but here the lineage from the harbi is established, so analogizing it to a pregnant woman from zina is not correct. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the 'iddah of a harbi (non-Muslim from enemy territory) woman who emigrates to the Muslims after embracing Islam. The author argues from the Quranic verse (Surah al-Mumtahanah 60:10) that the permission to marry these women is absolute, without mentioning 'iddah, so imposing 'iddah would be an addition to the text. The rational proof (dalil aqli) explains that 'iddah is meant to protect the husband's lineage (to avoid mixing of lineages). Since a harbi man's lineage is not honorable (he is like an animal, can be enslaved), his lineage does not deserve protection, so his wife does not observe 'iddah. An exception is made if she is pregnant: marriage is not permitted until delivery because the child's lineage is established and a second bed (marriage) would conflict with the existing bed. A narration from Imam Abu Hanifah that marrying her is permissible but intercourse is not (like a pregnant adulteress) is mentioned, but the preferred view is the impermissibility of marriage altogether, because the child's lineage from the harbi is established, unlike zina. Thus, the Hanafi position is clear: no 'iddah for a harbi convert, but if pregnant, wait until delivery.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): A waiting period incumbent upon a woman after divorce or death of husband to avoid mixing of lineages.
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war with Muslims, not under Muslim protection.
فراش (firash): The marital bed; legally, the husband's bed establishes the lineage of a child born during marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a woman from dar al-harb who becomes Muslim not observe 'iddah?
A) Because she is not required to protect her husband's lineage since he is a harbi.
B) Because she never had sexual relations with her husband.
C) Because the Quran explicitly says no 'iddah for them.
D) Because she is automatically divorced upon embracing Islam.

Key Takeaway
A harbi woman's 'iddah is waived because her husband's lineage is not protected by Islamic law, as he is not entitled to the honor of lineage preservation.

Hidad for the Mubtattah: Hanafi Proof and Shafi'i Rebuttal
States Hanafi position on hidad for mubtattah with proof and Shafi'i rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on hidad for a mubtattah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Hidad is wajib for both widow and mubtattah; the Prophet's prohibition of adornment applies to all women in 'iddah.

This passage addresses a key disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether a woman who has been irrevocably divorced must observe hidad (mourning restrictions). The Hanafi school extends the obligation beyond widows to include mubtattah women, supported by a general hadith and rational argument. Understanding this dispute clarifies the scope of 'iddah restrictions and the method of Hanafi istidlal.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that Hanafis hold hidad wajib for both mubtattah and widow, and note the source passage states this as 'our madhhab'.
2
Identify the opposing school's view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i argues hidad is only for widows, as it expresses regret for a husband who fulfilled his covenant until death.
3
Analyze the Hanafi textual proof
Examine the hadith cited: the Prophet forbade a woman in 'iddah from using henna, calling it perfume. This implies a general prohibition of adornment for all women in 'iddah, including mubtattah.
The hadith uses 'mu'taddah' which includes both divorced and widowed women.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rational proof
Understand the rational argument: separation is more painful than death because a woman could wash her husband's corpse before separation but not after. Thus hidad is even more appropriate for a mubtattah.
This is a qiyas that strengthens the textual proof.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical difference: Hanafis require the mubtattah to abstain from adornment and perfume during 'iddah; Shafi'is do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل قال وعلى المبتوتة والمتوفى عنها زوجها اذا كانت بالغة مسلمة الحداد اما المتوفى عنها زوجها فلقوله عليه السلام لا يحل لامرأة تومن بالله واليوم الأخران تحد على ميت فوق ثلثة ايام الاعلى زوجها اربعة اشهر و عشرا واما المبتوتة فمذهبنا وقال الشافعى لاحداد عليها لانه وجب اظهار اللتاسف على فوت زوج وفى. بعهدها الى مماته وقد او حشها بالابانة فلاتاسف بفوته ولناماروى ان النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى المعتدة ان تختضب بالحناء وقال الحناء طيب ولانه يجب اظهارا للتاسف على فوت نعمة النكاح الذى هو سبب لصونها وكفاية منها والابانة اقطع لها من الموت حتى كان لها ان تغسله ميتا قبل الابانة لابعدها
Chapter: He said: Upon the mubtattah (irrevocably divorced woman) and the one whose husband has died, if she is a mature Muslim woman, hidad is obligatory. As for the one whose husband has died, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to mourn for more than three days except for her husband: four months and ten days.' As for the mubtattah, it is our madhhab (that hidad is obligatory). Al-Shafi'i said: There is no hidad upon her because hidad is to express regret over the loss of a husband who fulfilled his covenant until his death, and he has isolated her by separation, so there is no regret in his loss. And we have the narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the woman in 'iddah from applying henna, and he said: 'Henna is perfume.' And because it is obligatory to express regret over the loss of the blessing of marriage, which is the cause of her protection and sufficiency, and separation is more cutting for her than death, such that she could wash him (bathe his corpse) before separation but not after.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the obligation of hidad (period of mourning with restrictions) for a woman who has received an irrevocable divorce (mubtattah). The Hanafi school holds that hidad is obligatory for both the mubtattah and the widow. The proof for the widow is the explicit hadith of the Prophet ﷺ. For the mubtattah, the Hanafis rely on a hadith where the Prophet forbade a woman in 'iddah (which includes both divorced and widowed) from using henna, considering it perfume. This indicates a general prohibition of adornment, i.e., hidad, for all women in 'iddah. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that hidad is only for a widow because it expresses regret for the loss of a husband who fulfilled his covenant. Since the mubtattah's husband has already separated from her, there is no reason to regret his death. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) The hadith prohibiting henna is general for all women in 'iddah, not specific. (2) Logically, separation is more painful than death because she could wash his corpse before separation (i.e., their bond was intact) but not after. Hence, expressing regret through hidad is even more appropriate for a mubtattah. The Hanafi position is thus established by both textual and rational evidence.

Key Terms
حداد (hidad): A period of mourning during which a woman refrains from adornment, perfume, and certain clothing.
مبتوتة (mubtattah): A woman who has been irrevocably divorced (either by three divorces, one bain divorce, or khul').
معتدة (mu'taddah): A woman who is observing 'iddah, whether due to divorce or death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary textual proof the Hanafis use for obligating hidad on an irrevocably divorced woman?
A) The hadith forbidding a woman in 'iddah from applying henna.
B) The Quranic verse on 'iddah.
C) Consensus of the companions.
D) Analogy to a widow.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates hidad on both widows and irrevocably divorced women, based on the general command to avoid adornment during 'iddah.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Obligation of Mourning (Hidad) for Widow and Irrevocably Divorced Woman
States ruling and proof for mourning obligation, refutes Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hidad for the mabtutah, cite the textual and rational proofs, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Mourning is wajib upon every woman in iddah, whether widow or irrevocably divorced, because separation cuts the marriage tie more than death.

In this lesson, we examine the obligation of mourning (hidad) during iddah. The Hanafi school holds that both the widow and the irrevocably divorced woman must abstain from adornments. The passage from Al-Hidayah presents the ruling, explains the textual and rational proofs, and refutes the Shafi'i position that distinguishes between the two.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the women subject to the ruling
The act is hidad (mourning by abstaining from adornments). The women are the widow (mutawaffa 'anha zawjaha) and the irrevocably divorced woman (mabtutah) – including triple divorce, bain divorce, and khul'.
2
Note the Hanafi ruling and the opponent's view
Hanafis rule it wajib for both. Imam Shafi'i holds it wajib only for the widow, not the mabtutah.
The disagreement is on the mabtutah.
3
Examine the first proof: general hadiths
The hadith from Umm Salamah forbids a woman in iddah from using henna (perfume) without distinguishing between widow and divorced. Another narration by Tahawi lists four types of women who must refrain, including the mabtutah.
The texts are general ('amm) and thus include all women in iddah.
4
Examine the rational proof (qiyas)
Analogy (qiyas) annexes the mabtutah to the widow: the reason for hidad is grief over loss of the marriage blessing. Separation (bain) severs the tie more completely than death – e.g., a wife can wash her deceased husband but not after bain divorce. Therefore, mourning is even more warranted.
This refutes Shafi'i's objection that the husband failed to fulfill the contract.
5
Understand the practical difference
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a mabtutah in the Hanafi school must avoid perfume, kohl, dyed clothes, and leaving home unnecessarily during iddah, while in the Shafi'i school she may adorn herself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العدة
جو عورت اللہ اور روز قیامت پر ایمان رکھنے اس کو حلال نہیں ہے کہ تین دن سے زیادہ کسی مرد پر سوگ کرے سوائے اپنے شوہر کے کہ اس پر چار ماہ دس یوم سوگ کرے ) اور رہی مبہو نہ تو یہ ہمارا مذہب ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اس پر سوگ لازم نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ سوگ کرنا تو ایسے شوہر کے فوت ہونے پر تاسف ظاہر کرنے کے لئے ہوتا ہے جس نے اپنے مرنے تک اس عورت کا معاہد ہ پورا کیا ہو حالانکہ اس شخص نے جدا کر کے اس کو وحشت میں دال دیا تو اس کی جدائی پر سوگ سے تأسف لازم نہیں ہے اور ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں روایت کیا گیا کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے معدہ کو رنگ حنا استعمال کرنے سے منع کیا ہے اور فرمایا کہ حنا خوشبو ہے اور اس لئے کہ سوگ اس نعمت نکاح کے فوت ہونے پر تاسف ظاہر کرنے کے لئے واجب ہوتا ہے جو اس عورت کی حفاظت اور اس کی ضروریات کی کفایت کا سبب تھا اور جدائی واقع ہوناعورت کے حق میں شوہر کے مرنے سے زیادہ گھبراہت کی چیز ہے چنانچہ جدائی سے پہلے وہ اپنے مردار شو ہر کونسل دے سکتی ہے نہ کہ جدائی کے بعد ۔
تشریح ماسبق میں نفس وجوب عدت اور کیفیت وجوب عدت کو بیان کیا گیا ہے اور کن عورتوں پر عدت واجب ہو گی اور کن پر نہیں اس کو بیان کیا گیا ہے۔ اس فصل میں مصنف ہدا یہ ان چیزوں کو ذکر کریں گے جن کا کرنا معدات پر واجب ہے اور جن کا نہ کرنا واجب ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ متونہ یعنی وہ عورت جس سے حق رجعت منقطع ہو گیا ہو خواہ تین طلاقیں دی گئی ہوں یا ایک طلاق بائنہ واقع کی گئی ہویا خلع کیا گیا ہو اور وہ عورت جس کا شوہر وفات پا گیا ہوا اگر یہ مسلمان بالغہ ہیں تو ان پر سوگ کرنا واجب ہے۔ متوفی عنہا ز وجھا پر سوگ واجب ہونے میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حدیث ہے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جو عورت اللہ اور قیامت کے دن پر ایمان لائی اس کے لئے کسی میت پر تین دن سے زیادہ سوگ کرنا حلال نہیں ہے سوائے اس کے کہ اپنے شوہر پر چار ماہ دس روز تک سوگ کر سکتی ہے۔ اور رہی مبہو نہ تو اس پر سوگ کا واجب ہونا ہمارامذ استعمال کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے اور فرمایا کہ حنا خوشبو ہے اس حدیث کی راویہ حضرت ام سلمہ ہیں اور اس حدیث میں معتدہ وفات اور معتدہ غیر وفات کی تفصیل نہیں کی گئی ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ مطلقا معتدہ پر سوگ کرنا واجب ہے۔ معتدہ وفات ہو یا معتدہ غیر وفات ہو۔ اس کے ہم معنی ایک اور روایت امام طحاوی نے نقل کی ہے جس کی سند حماد عن ابراہیم انتھی ہے الفاظ حدیث یہ ہیں : قال المطلقة والمختلعة و المتوفى عنها زوجها والملاعنة لا يختضبن و لا يتطيبن ولا يلبسن ثوبا مصبوغا و لا يخرجن من بيوتهن ۔ یعنی فرمایا کہ مطلقہ اور جس سے ضلع کیا گیا ہے اور جس کا شوہر مر گیا اور جس سے لعان کیا گیا ہے یہ سب عورتیں خضاب نہ کریں اور نہ خوشبولگائیں اور نہ رنگا ہوا کپڑا پہنیں اور نہ اپنے گھروں سے نکلیں۔ دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ مبتو تہ کو متوفیٰ عنہا ز وجھا کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا جائے اور تقریریہ کی جائے کہ متوفی عنہاز و جھا پر سوگ واجب ہونے پر نص وارد ہوئی ہے جیسا کہ ابھی حدیث گذری ہے اور سوگ واجب ہونے کی وجہ اس نعمت بآج کے فوت ہونے پر اظہار افسوس کرنا ہے جو اس عورت کی حفاظت اور ضروریات کی کفایت کا سبب ہے اور بینونت واقع ہو نا عورت کے حق کو شوہر کی موت سے زیادہ قطع کرنے والا ہے کیونکہ نکاح کا حکم وفات کے بعد عدت گزرنے تک باقی رہتا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ عورت اپنے مردہ شوہر کو بائنہ کرنے سے پہلے قسل دے سکتی ہے مگر بائنہ کرنے کے بعد اگر مر گیا تو اس کو یہ عورت غسل نہیں دے سکتی۔ پس جب متو تہ کومتوفی عنہا ز وجھا کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا تو جو حکم متوفی عنہا ز وجھا کا ہے وہی مبتو تہ کا ہوگا یعنی دونوں پر سوگ کرنا واجب ہے۔
Chapter of Iddah. A woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day, it is not permissible for her to mourn for any deceased more than three days except for her husband, for whom she may mourn four months and ten days. As for the irrevocably divorced woman, this is our madhhab, and Imam Shafi'i said that mourning is not obligatory upon her, because mourning is to express regret at the death of a husband who fulfilled his contract until his death, whereas this man separated her and left her in distress, so regret at his separation is not required. Our proof is the hadith in which it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade a woman in iddah from applying henna dye and said that henna is perfume. And because mourning is wajib to express regret at the loss of the blessing of marriage, which was the cause of her protection and provision; and separation occurring is more disturbing for a woman than the death of a husband. Thus, before separation she can wash her deceased husband, not after separation. Commentary: In the preceding, the essence of the obligation of iddah and its modality were explained, and which women must observe iddah and which not. In this chapter, the author of Hidayah will mention those things that are obligatory for women in iddah and those that are prohibited. So he said: 'Mabtutah' - a woman whose right of return (raj'ah) is severed, whether by triple divorce, a single irrevocable divorce, or khul', and a woman whose husband has died, if they are Muslim adults, then mourning is wajib upon them. For the widow, there is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'A woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day, it is not permissible for her to mourn any deceased more than three days, except for her husband, for four months and ten days.' As for the mabtutah, its wajib is our madhhab, while Imam Shafi'i says it is not wajib. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that mourning is to express regret at the death of a husband who fulfilled his contract until his death, whereas this man made her separated and distressed, so there is no regret at his death. Our proof is that the Prophet forbade a woman in iddah from using henna dye and said henna is perfume. This hadith is narrated by Umm Salamah, and it does not differentiate between a widow and a divorced woman. Therefore, it is established that mourning is wajib for every woman in iddah, whether widow or non-widow. Another similar narration is reported by Imam Tahawi: 'Al-mutallaqah, al-mukhtala'ah, al-mutawaffa 'anha zawjaha, and al-mula'anah do not dye, apply perfume, wear dyed garments, or leave their homes.' Rational proof: The mabtutah is annexed to the widow, and it is clarified that for the widow, mourning is wajib by text as in the hadith. The reason for mourning is to express regret at the loss of the blessing that was the cause of her protection and provision. And separation is more severing for the woman than death, because the effect of marriage persists after death until the iddah ends. This is why a woman may wash her deceased husband before separation, but not after. Thus, when the mabtutah is annexed to the widow, the same ruling applies: both must observe mourning.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi perspective, expanding on the Hidayah. It addresses the obligation of mourning (hidad) for two types of women: the widow (mutawaffa 'anha zawjaha) and the irrevocably divorced woman (mabtutah), i.e., one who has received a bain divorce or khul'. The author states that for both, mourning is wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school. The primary proof is a hadith narrated by Umm Salamah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade a woman in iddah from using henna, and henna is perfume. This applies generally to all women in iddah without exception, so it includes both widow and divorced woman. A second hadith from Imam Tahawi lists four categories of women (divorcée, khul', widow, and woman divorced by li'an) who must refrain from adornment. The rational proof follows: since mourning is for expressing grief over the loss of the blessing of marriage (which provided protection and sustenance), and separation through irrevocable divorce is even more severe than death (because the marriage tie is cut more completely—a wife can wash her husband before divorce but not after), by analogy the mabtutah is likened to the widow, and the same obligation applies. The passage also refutes Imam Shafi'i's view that mourning is not wajib for the mabtutah because the husband failed to fulfill the marriage contract till death. The Hanafi response is that the purpose of mourning is to show grief at the loss of the marriage blessing, and separation cuts that tie even more strongly, so mourning is even more appropriate. The authority weight: This is from the Hidayah sharh, relying on Zahir al-Riwayah through the hadith and the rulings of Imam Muhammad and others.

Key Terms
مبتوتة (mabtutah): A woman who has been irrevocably divorced (bain), including by three divorces, khul', or one bain divorce.
الحداد (al-hidad): Mourning, specifically abstaining from adornments like perfume, kohl, dyed clothes, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following women must observe mourning (hidad) during her iddah?
A) Only the widow
B) Only the irrevocably divorced woman
C) Both the widow and the irrevocably divorced woman
D) Neither the widow nor the divorced woman

Key Takeaway
Both the widow and the irrevocably divorced woman must observe hidad during their iddah.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Hidad for Disbeliever, Minor, and Slave Woman
Explains hidad rulings for disbeliever, minor, slave woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hidad for a disbelieving woman, a minor girl, and a slave woman, and explain the proof and the inter-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Hidad is wajib only for Muslim adult women who have lost a valid marital blessing; disbelievers and minors are exempt, but slave women are obligated.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies the obligation of mourning (hidad) during iddah for three categories: disbelieving women, minor girls, and slave women. The commentator explains the reasoning behind each ruling and addresses the disagreement with Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly applying the obligation of hidad in different scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories and their rulings
From the text, list the three categories: disbelieving woman (no hidad), minor girl (no hidad), slave woman in iddah of death or irrevocable divorce (hidad wajib).
The slave woman's ruling is conditional on her iddah being for death or irrevocable divorce.
2
Examine the proof for the disbelieving woman
The text cites the hadith 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day...' to show that hidad is only for believers. Also, a disbeliever is not addressed by the divine rights of Shari'ah.
The hadith is a dalil naqli.
3
Examine the proof for the minor girl
The minor is not mukallaf; the divine address (khitab) is lifted from her, so she is not obligated.
This is based on the general principle of taklif.
4
Examine the proof for the slave woman
The slave woman is addressed by all legal rights that do not void her master's right of service. Since hidad does not void the master's right, it is wajib. The contrast is made with the prohibition of leaving the house, which would void the master's right.
The reasoning uses a comparison (qiyas) between hidad and the prohibition of leaving the house.
5
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i hold that hidad is wajib for a disbelieving woman and a minor. The Hanafi response is that the hadith specifies faith, and the minor is not mukallaf.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is that a Hanafi mufti would not require hidad from these women, while a Shafi'i mufti would.

Source Text

حق باطل نہیں ہوتا بخلاف باہر جانے کی ممانعت کیونکہ اس میں مولی کا حق باطل ہو جاتا ہے اور بندہ کا حق اس کی حاجت کی وجہ سے مقدم کیا گیا ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں ان معتدات کا ذکر کیا ہے جن پر سوگ واجب نہیں ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ کا فرعورت پر سوگ نہیں ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ کا فر حقوق الہی کی مخاطب نہیں ہے اور سوگ اللہ کے حقوق میں سے ہے چنانچہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حدیث لا يحل لامرأة تومن بالله واليوم الآخر میں اسی طرف اشارہ کیا گیا ہے۔ البتہ امام مالک اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ کافرہ عورت پر بھی سوگ واجب ہے اور صغیر پر بھی سوگ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ خطاب الہی کو اس پر سے اٹھا لیا گیا ہے۔ یعنی وہ خطاب الہی میں داخل ہی نہیں ہوئی اور امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس پر بھی سوگ واجب ہے۔ اور باندی اگر عدت وفات یا طلاق بائن کی عدت میں ہو تو اس پر بھی سوگ کرنا واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ باندی ان تمام حقوق شرع کی مخاطب ہوتی ہے جن میں اس کے مولیٰ کا حق باطل نہ ہوتا ہو اور سوگ کرنا ایسی ہی چیز ہے جس میں اسکے مولیٰ کا حق باطل نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اور برخلاف گھر سے باہر نکلنے کی ممانعت کے۔ یعنی باندی کو عدت کے زما نہ میں گھر سے باہر نکلنے کی اجازت حاصل ہوگی۔ کیونکہ گھر سے باہر نکلنے کی ممانعت کی صورت میں مولیٰ کا حق استخدام باطل ہو جاتا ہے اور چونکہ مولی ایک بند بھتاج[؟] ہے۔ یعنی اس کو اپنی باندی سے خدمت لینے کی حاجت پڑتی ہے تو اس کی حاجت کو حق شرع پر مقدم کیا۔
ام ولد کی عدت میں اور نکاح فاسد کی عدت میں سوگ نہیں
قال وليس فى عدة ام الولد ولا فى عدة النكاح الفاسد احداد لانها ما فاتها نعمة النكاح لتظهر التاسف والاباحة اصل
ترجمہ اور ام ولد کی عدت میں اور نکاح فاسد کی عدت میں سوگ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان عورتوں میں سے کسی کی نعمت نکاح زائل نہیں ہوئی ہے۔ تا کہ افسوس کرنا ظاہر ہوتا اور مباح ہونا اصل ہے۔ تشریح اگر ام ولد کے مولیٰ نے ام ولد کو آزاد کیا یا مولی مرگیا تو ام ولد پر اس کی عدت میں سوگ واجب نہیں ہے اور اگر کوئی عورت نکاح فاسد میں جدا ہوئی تو اس کی عدت میں بھی سوگ نہیں ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ سوگ واجب ہوتا ہے نعمت نکاح زائل ہونے کی وجہ سے اور یہاں ان عورتوں میں سے کسی کی نعمت نکاح زائل نہیں ہوئی۔ تا کہ سوگ سے اس کا اظہار واجب ہوتا اور اصل یہ ہے کہ عورت اپنے آپ کو آراستہ کرے۔ یعنی سوگ نہ کرے۔ اسلئے حکم اپنی اصل پر باقی رہے گا۔
The right does not become void, contrary to the prohibition of going out because in that the master's right becomes void, and the slave's right due to his need is given precedence. Commentary: In this passage, mention is made of those women in iddah upon whom mourning is not obligatory. Thus he said: There is no mourning for a disbelieving woman. The proof is that a disbeliever is not addressed by the divine rights, and mourning is among the rights of Allah. Accordingly, the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day...' points to this. However, Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i said that mourning is obligatory even for a disbelieving woman. And there is no mourning for a minor because the divine address is lifted from her; i.e., she is not included in the divine address. According to Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i, mourning is obligatory for her as well. And if a slave woman is in the iddah of death or irrevocable divorce, mourning is obligatory upon her because she is addressed by all the legal rights in which the master's right does not become void, and mourning is something in which the master's right does not become void. Contrary to the prohibition of leaving the house, i.e., the slave woman will have permission to leave the house during her iddah because in the case of prohibition of leaving the house, the master's right of service becomes void. Since the master is a needy person [؟], i.e., he has need of taking service from his slave woman, his need is given precedence over the legal right. There is no mourning in the iddah of umm walad and in the iddah of a fasid marriage. He said: There is no mourning in the iddah of umm walad nor in the iddah of a fasid marriage because the blessing of marriage has not ceased for them so that regret could be shown, and permissibility is the original rule. Translation: And there is no mourning in the iddah of umm walad and in the iddah of a fasid marriage because the blessing of marriage has not ceased for any of these women so that showing regret would be obligatory, and permissibility is the original rule. Commentary: If the master of the umm walad freed her or the master died, then during her iddah mourning is not obligatory. And if a woman separates due to a fasid marriage, there is no mourning in her iddah. The proof is that mourning becomes obligatory due to the cessation of the blessing of marriage, and here the blessing of marriage has not ceased for any of these women so that its display through mourning would be obligatory. The original rule is that a woman adorns herself, i.e., she does not mourn. Therefore the ruling remains on its original basis.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage discusses the obligation of hidad (mourning) for different categories of women in iddah. The commentator explains that the original text states that a disbelieving woman is not required to observe mourning because she is not addressed by the divine commands regarding Islamic rituals. This is supported by the hadith that restricts mourning to women who believe in Allah and the Last Day. However, Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i disagree and hold that mourning is obligatory even for disbelieving women. For a minor girl, there is no mourning because she is not legally responsible. The slave woman, on the other hand, must observe mourning if she is in the iddah of death or irrevocable divorce because she is addressed by the Shar'i rulings that do not conflict with her master's rights. Mourning does not hamper the master's right of service, unlike the prohibition of leaving the house, which would prevent the master from utilizing her services. Therefore, the slave's need to provide service is given precedence. Then the passage covers umm walad and fasid marriage. The ruling is that there is no mourning for a umm walad whose master died or freed her, nor for a woman who separates due to a fasid marriage, because the blessing of marriage did not truly cease (for umm walad, she was a concubine; for fasid nikah, the marriage was invalid from the start). Since the cause for mourning (loss of marital blessing) is absent, the original permissibility of adornment remains.

Key Terms
سوگ (hidad): Mourning by avoiding adornment, perfume, and beautification during the iddah period.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband.
مخاطب (mukhatab): One who is addressed by the divine command; legally responsible (mukallaf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following women is REQUIRED to observe hidad (mourning) according to the Hanafi school?
A) A disbelieving woman in iddah of death
B) A minor girl in iddah of death
C) A slave woman in iddah of death or irrevocable divorce
D) An umm walad after her master's death

Key Takeaway
Hidad is not wajib for disbelievers and minors due to lack of taklif, but it is wajib for slave women because the obligation does not conflict with the master's rights.

Hidad for Umm Walad and Fasid Marriage
Explains no hidad for umm walad and fasid marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why umm walad and a woman in a fasid marriage are not required to observe hidad, citing the ratio legis of loss of marital blessing.

Core Idea
Hidad is only owed when a valid marital blessing is lost; for umm walad and fasid marriage, no such blessing existed or was lost.

This passage concludes the discussion on hidad by addressing two more categories: the umm walad (a slave woman who bore a child to her master) and a woman who separates due to an invalid (fasid) marriage. The commentator explains that since the loss of the blessing of a valid marriage is the cause for hidad, and these women did not have that blessing, the obligation drops. The original rule of permissibility of adornment remains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories and their ruling
The text mentions umm walad (whose master freed her or died) and a woman in fasid marriage. For both, there is no hidad.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the umm walad is freed or the master dies.
2
Understand the ratio legis
Hidad becomes wajib due to the cessation of the blessing of a valid marriage (ni'mat al-nikah). For the umm walad, she never had a valid marriage with her master; she was a concubine. For the fasid marriage, the marriage was invalid from the start, so no blessing was ever established.
The cause (illa) is the loss of the blessing of a valid marriage.
3
Apply the default rule
The original rule (asl) is that a woman may adorn herself. Since the cause for hidad is absent, the ruling remains on its default: no hidad.
This is a case of istishab: retaining the original permissibility.

Commentary: In this passage, mention is made of those women in iddah upon whom mourning is not obligatory. Thus he said: There is no mourning for a disbelieving woman. The proof is that a disbeliever is not addressed by the divine rights, and mourning is among the rights of Allah. Accordingly, the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day...' points to this. However, Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i said that mourning is obligatory even for a disbelieving woman. And there is no mourning for a minor because the divine address is lifted from her; i.e., she is not included in the divine address. According to Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i, mourning is obligatory for her as well. And if a slave woman is in the iddah of death or irrevocable divorce, mourning is obligatory upon her because she is addressed by all the legal rights in which the master's right does not become void, and mourning is something in which the master's right does not become void. Contrary to the prohibition of leaving the house, i.e., the slave woman will have permission to leave the house during her iddah because in the case of prohibition of leaving the house, the master's right of service becomes void. Since the master is a needy person [؟], i.e., he has need of taking service from his slave woman, his need is given precedence over the legal right. There is no mourning in the iddah of umm walad and in the iddah of a fasid marriage. He said: There is no mourning in the iddah of umm walad nor in the iddah of a fasid marriage because the blessing of marriage has not ceased for them so that regret could be shown, and permissibility is the original rule. Commentary: If the master of the umm walad freed her or the master died, then during her iddah mourning is not obligatory. And if a woman separates due to a fasid marriage, there is no mourning in her iddah. The proof is that mourning becomes obligatory due to the cessation of the blessing of marriage, and here the blessing of marriage has not ceased for any of these women so that its display through mourning would be obligatory. The original rule is that a woman adorns herself, i.e., she does not mourn. Therefore the ruling remains on its original basis.

This passage discusses the obligation of hidad (mourning) for different categories of women in iddah. Key Terms
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master, becoming free upon his death.
نکاح فاسد (nikah fasid): An invalid marriage due to a missing condition or prohibited element, such as lack of witnesses or marrying a mahram.
نعمت نکاح (ni'mat al-nikah): The blessing of a valid marriage, including the rights and companionship, whose loss is mourned through hidad.

Leaving the House During Iddah: Divorced vs. Widow
Distinguishing rulings for divorced vs. widowed women in iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on leaving the house for a divorced woman (raj'iyya or bain) and a widow during iddah, and identify the Quranic evidence for each.

Core Idea
A divorced woman must stay home day and night; a widow may go out for livelihood.

The iddah period imposes different restrictions depending on the cause of separation. The Quranic text (Surah al-Talaq 65:1) strictly confines the divorced woman, while the widow is granted flexibility due to financial necessity. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the rationale behind the distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage discusses two types of women in iddah: the divorced woman (both raj'iyya and bain) and the widow (mutawaffa 'anha zawjuha). Note the distinct rulings for each.
2
State the ruling for each category
For the divorced woman: prohibited from leaving the house at any time (night or day). For the widow: permitted to leave during the day and part of the night, but must not spend the night outside her home.
3
Locate the Quranic evidence
The passage cites Surah al-Talaq 65:1: 'Do not expel them from their houses, nor let them leave unless they commit a clear immoral act.' Identify the verse's direct application to the divorced woman.
The Hanafis interpret 'fahisha' either as the act of leaving itself or as adultery, both reinforcing the prohibition.
4
Understand the rationale for the widow's permission
The widow has no maintenance (nafaqa) from the deceased husband's estate, so she needs to go out to earn a living. The divorced woman receives maintenance, hence she does not share the same need.
There is an ikhtilaf if the divorced woman forfeits her maintenance: some say she may then go out during the day.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطلقہ رجعیہ اور مبہو نہ کارات اور دن کو گھر سے نکلنا نا جائز ہے اور متوفی عنہاز و جہادن کو نکل سکتی ہے اور رات کے بعض حصے کو نکل سکتی ہے
ولا يجوز للمطلقة الرجعية والمتبوتة الخروج من بيتها ليلا ولا نهار او المتوفى عنها زوجها تخرج نهارا وبعض الليل ولاتبيت فى غير منزلها اما المطلقة فلقوله تعالى ولا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن ولا يخرجن الاان ياتين بفاحشة مبينة قيل الفاحشة نفس الخروج وقيل الزناء ويخرجن لاقامة الحدواما المتوفى عنها زوجها فلانه لا نفقة لها فيحتاج الى الخروج نهار الطلب المعاش وقديمتد الى ان يهجم الليل ولا كذلك المطلقة لان النفقة دارة عليها من مال زوجها حتى لو اختلعت على نفقة عدتها قيل انها تخرج نهارا وقيل لا تخرج لانها اسقطت حقها فلا يبطل به حق عليها
ترجمہ اور جس عورت کو طلاق رجعی دی گئی یا بائن دی گئی (اس کو اپنے گھر سے نکلنا رات یا دن میں جائز نہیں ہے اور جس کا شوہر مر گیا
It is not permissible for a woman given a revocable (raj'iyya) or irrevocable (bain) divorce to leave her house night or day. As for a woman whose husband has died, she may leave during the day and part of the night, but she should not spend the night in a place other than her house. As for the divorced woman, because Allah says: 'Do not expel them from their houses, nor let them leave unless they commit a clear immoral act.' It is said that the immoral act is the very act of leaving, and it is said it is adultery. And they leave for the establishment of hudud (Islamic penalties). As for the woman whose husband has died, because she has no maintenance, so she needs to go out during the day to seek a livelihood, and it may extend until night falls. The divorced woman is not like that because maintenance is due to her from her husband's wealth. Even if she consented to forgo the maintenance of her iddah, it is said that she may leave during the day, and it is said she may not leave because she waived her right, so a right is not invalidated by it. Translation: And a woman given a revocable or irrevocable divorce is not allowed to leave her house night or day, and the one whose husband has died... [cut off]
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage explains the difference in mobility for women in iddah depending on the cause. A divorced woman (whether raj'iyya or bain) is prohibited from leaving her house entirely during the iddah period, both day and night, based on the Quranic command (Surah al-Talaq 65:1). She may only leave for a valid necessity like establishing a hadd punishment. The widow, however, is permitted to go out during the day and part of the night to earn a livelihood because she does not receive maintenance from her deceased husband's estate. However, she must not spend the night away from her home. The commentary also discusses a scenario where the divorced woman forfeits her maintenance: there is a difference of opinion whether she may then go out. The Hanafi position generally maintains the prohibition for the divorced woman regardless.

Key Terms
مطلقة رجعية (mutallaqa raj'iyya): A woman divorced with a revocable divorce, meaning her husband can take her back during the iddah without a new contract.
مطلقة بائن (mutallaqa bain): A woman divorced irrevocably; the husband cannot take her back except with a new contract.
متوفى عنها زوجها (mutawaffa 'anha zawjuha): A widow whose husband has died.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, which scenario is permitted?
A) A divorced woman (bāʾin) leaving her house at night to buy groceries.
B) A widow staying overnight at her sister's house.
C) A widow going out during the day to work and returning home before night.
D) A divorced woman (rajʿiyya) leaving during the day to visit her parents.

Key Takeaway
The divorced woman's prohibition from leaving the house is derived from the Quranic text and her entitlement to maintenance, while the widow's permission is based on necessity due to the lack of maintenance.

Ruling on a Woman in Iddah Leaving Her Home – Distinguishing Divorcee and Widow
Explains the different rulings for divorcees and widows regarding leaving the house during iddah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a divorcee and a widow during iddah regarding leaving the house, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the interpretation of 'fāḥishah' in Qur'an 65:1.

Core Idea
A divorcee must stay home; a widow may go out by day for work – the difference is maintenance (nafaqah).

This passage addresses the critical question of when a woman in iddah may leave her home. The Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction between a divorcee and a widow, based on the presence or absence of financial support (nafaqah). For the divorcee, the Qur'anic command is strict, yet there is a notable intra-Hanafi disagreement on what constitutes the exception of 'fāḥishah'. For the widow, necessity permits daytime leaving, but she must return by night.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Recognize that the passage separately addresses a divorcee (revocable or irrevocable) and a widow. Each has a different ruling regarding leaving the house during iddah.
The divorcee includes both raj'ī and ba'in.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the Quranic verse (65:1) that prohibits turning out or leaving except for a clear immorality (fāḥishah). Determine its role as the proof for the divorcee's restriction.
The verse is the core evidence.
3
Analyze the exception (fāḥishah)
Examine the three interpretations within the Hanafi school: leaving itself, adultery, or disobedience. Understand how each interpretation changes the ruling on when a divorcee may be expelled.
This is the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Compare the rationale for the widow
The widow has no nafaqah, so she needs to go out to earn a livelihood. This necessity permits daytime leaving, but she must return by night.
The absence of maintenance is the key distinction.
5
Note the khul' issue
The passage mentions a secondary ikhtilaf: if a divorcee makes khul' on her iddah maintenance, some say she may go out by day, others say not.
This reinforces the link between nafaqah and permission.

باب العدة
ہو وہ دن بھر اور کچھ رات تک نکل سکتی ہے۔ (لیکن) اپنے گھر کے علاوہ میں رات نہ گزارے۔
بہر حال مطلقہ (کے واسطے اس حکم کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے ولا تخرجوهن .... الآية _ یعنی ان عورتوں کو ان کے رہنے کے ) گھروں سے مر نکالو اور نہ وہ عورتیں خود نکلیں مگر ہاں کوئی کھلی بے حیائی کریں ۔ ( تو اور بات ہے ) بیان القرآن اور بعض نے کہا کہ فاحشہ نفس خروج ہے اور کہا گیا کہ زنا ہے اور نکلیں گی اقامت حد کے واسطے رہی وہ عورت جس کا شوہر مر گیا تو اسلئے کہ اس کا کچھ نفقہ نہیں۔ پس دن میں روزی تلاش کرنے کیلئے نکلنے کی محتاج ہے اور کبھی طلب معاش رات کے آنے تک دراز - جاتا ہے اور مطلقہ ایسی نہیں۔ کیونکہ نفقہ برابر اس کے شوہر کے مال سے اس پر جاری رہتا ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر اس نے اپنی عدت کے نفقہ پر ضلع کیا تو بعض حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ دن میں نکلے گی اور بعض کہتے ہیں کہ نہیں نکلے گی۔ اسلئے کہ اس نے اپنا حق (خود) ساقط کر دیا۔ پس اس کی وجہ سے وہ حق باطل نہیں ہوگا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جس عورت کو طلاق رجعی یا طلاق بائن دی گئی وہ رات یا دن میں اس مکان سے باہر نہ نکلے جس میں وہ مفارقت کے وقت رہتی تھی۔ ہاں اگر وہ نکلنے پر مجبور ہو جائے ( مثلاً مکان کے گرنے کا اندیشہ ہے یا اپنی جان یا مال پر غارت گری کا خطرہ ہے یا مالک مکان اس کو نکال دے مثلا کرایہ پر رہتی تھی اور اب کرایہ ادا کرنے کی قدرت نہیں ) تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ۔ اور متوفی عنہا زوجہا کیلئے دن بھر اور رات کا کچھ حصہ گھر سے باہر رہنے کی شرعاً اجازت ہے۔ البتہ رات اپنے مکان عدت ہی میں گزارے۔ اس کے علاوہ میں رات گزارنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔ پس مطلقہ عورت کیلئے گھر سے باہر نہ نکلنے پر دلیل اللہ تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے واتقو الله ربكم لا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن ولا يخرجن الا ان ياتين بفاحشة مبينة یعنی تم اللہ تعالیٰ سے ڈرتے رہو جو تمہارا رب ہے۔ ان عورتوں کو ان کے رہنے کے گھروں سے مت نکالو ( کیونکہ سکنی مطلقہ کا مثل منکوحہ کے واجب ہے ) اور نہ وہ عورتیں خود نکلیں مگر ہاں کوئی کھلی بے حیائی کریں تو اور بات ہے۔
مثلاً بدکاری کا ارتکاب کیا ہو یا چوری کی ہو تو سزا کیلئے نکالی جاویں۔ یا بقول بعض علماء زبان درازی اور ہر وقت کا رنج و تکرار رکھتی ہوں تو ان کو نکال دینا جائز ہے۔ (بیان القرآن ) لفظ فاحشہ کی تفسیر میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے۔ بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ فاحشہ سے مراد نفس خروج ہے۔ یہ قول ابراہیم مخفی کا ہے اور اسی کو اختیار کیا ہے امام اعظم ابو حنیفہ نے۔ اس صورت میں آیت کے معنی ہوں گے کہ معندہ عورتیں اپنے گھروں سے نہ نکلیں مگر یہ کہ ان کا نکلنا فاحشہ یعنی بے حیائی کی بات ہوگی۔ یہ ایسا ہے جیسے کہا جاتا ہے لا يسب النبی عليه السلام الا كافر ولا يزنى احد الا ان يكون فاسقاً یعنی نبی علیہ السلام کو گالی دینا کفر ہے اور زنا کر نافستق ہے اور بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ فاحشہ سے مراد زنا ہے۔ اب مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ معدہ عورتیں نہ نکلیں ۔ ہاں اگر انہوں نے زنا کا ارتکاب کیا ہو تو حد جاری کرنے کیلئے ان کو نکالا جائے گا۔ یہ قول ہے ابن مسعود کا اور اس کو اختیار کیا ہے امام ابو یوسف نے اور ابن عباس نے فرمایا کہ فاحشہ سے مراد عورت کا ناشزہ اور نا فرمان ہونا ہے۔ اور متوفی عنہاز و جہا کے دن بھر اور رات کے کچھ حصہ گھر سے باہر رہنے کی اجازت پر دلیل یہ ہے کہ متوفی عنہاز و جہا کے واسطے نفقہ نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اس کو طلب معاش کیلئے گھر سے باہر رہنے کی ضرورت ہے اور چونکہ بسا اوقات کام کرتے کرتے رات آ جاتی ہے اور کچھ حصہ رات کا گذر بھی جاتا ہے۔ اسلئے دن کے ساتھ رات کے کچھ حصہ تک باہر رہنے کی اجازت دی گئی ہے۔
It is not permissible for a woman given revocable divorce (raj'ī) or irrevocable divorce (ba'in) to leave her house by night or day. But a woman whose husband has died may go out during the day and part of the night, and she may not spend the night outside her home. As for the divorcee, the proof is Allah's saying: "Do not turn them out of their houses, nor shall they leave, unless they commit a clear immorality" (Qur'an 65:1). It is said that the immorality (fāḥishah) is the act of leaving itself, and it is said it is adultery. They are taken out for the execution of the legal punishment. As for the widow, because she has no maintenance (nafaqah), she needs to go out during the day to seek a livelihood, and it may extend until nightfall. The divorcee is not like that because maintenance is due to her from her husband's wealth. Even if she has made a khul' (divorce by compensation) on the maintenance of her iddah, some say she goes out during the day, and some say she does not, because she has dropped her right, so that right is not nullified by it. Commentary: The issue is that a woman given revocable or irrevocable divorce should not leave the house she lived in at the time of separation by night or day. However, if she is compelled (e.g., fear of the house collapsing, danger to life or property, or the landlord evicts her because she cannot pay rent), then there is no harm. As for the widow, she is permitted by Sharia to be outside during the day and part of the night, but she must spend the night in her iddah residence. For the divorcee, the proof is the verse "Fear Allah, your Lord. Do not turn them out of their houses, nor shall they leave, unless they commit a clear immorality." For example, if she commits fornication or theft, she is taken out for punishment. Or, according to some scholars, if she is abusive and quarrelsome, it is permissible to evict her. There is disagreement on the interpretation of 'fāḥishah': some say it means the act of leaving itself (Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, adopted by Imam Abu Hanifa), others say it means adultery (Ibn Mas'ud, adopted by Imam Abu Yusuf), and Ibn Abbas said it means the woman's nushūz (disobedience). For the widow, the proof is that she has no maintenance, so she needs to go out to seek livelihood, and sometimes work extends into the night, so she is permitted to be out during the day and part of the night.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage addresses the rules for a woman in iddah leaving her home. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a divorcee (revocable or irrevocable) and a widow. For a divorcee, the general rule is that she must remain in the house where she was living at the time of separation, based on Qur'an 65:1. She is not allowed to go out except in cases of necessity (e.g., danger) or if she commits a clear immorality (fāḥishah). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the interpretation of 'fāḥishah': Imam Abu Hanifa interprets it as the act of leaving itself, meaning her leaving is itself immoral and thus grounds for being taken out; Imam Abu Yusuf, following Ibn Mas'ud, interprets it as adultery, meaning she is taken out for execution of the hadd punishment; and Ibn Abbas interprets it as nushūz (disobedience). The second part discusses the widow: she is allowed to go out during the day and part of the night because she has no maintenance, so she must work. However, she must return home by night. This concession is based on necessity. The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, with the ikhtilaf noted within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
فاحشة (fāḥishah): A clear immoral act; in this context, it is subject to different interpretations: leaving the house (Abu Hanifa), adultery (Abu Yusuf), or disobedience (Ibn Abbas).
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance or financial support due to a wife or divorcee during iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a widow allowed to go out during the day while a revocable divorcee must stay home?
A) The widow has no maintenance so she must work.
B) The divorcee is prohibited by Quranic text, while the widow is not mentioned.
C) The widow has permission from her deceased husband.
D) The divorcee is considered still married.

Key Takeaway
The key distinction is maintenance (nafaqah): a divorcee is maintained and must stay home; a widow must earn and may go out by day.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling on Leaving the House During 'Iddah: Divorced Women and Widows
Explains rulings on leaving house during 'iddah for divorced and widowed women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the house during 'iddah for divorced women and widows, and explain the difference based on their financial situation.

Core Idea
A divorced woman must stay home day and night; a widow may leave by day for sustenance but must return by night.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary explains a crucial distinction in 'iddah residency: the divorced woman (muttalaqah) and the widow (mutawaffa 'anha) have different rules regarding leaving the house. While both must generally remain in the marital home, the widow's need for income creates a concession. We'll examine the legal proof and rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Separate the rulings for a divorced woman (muttalaqah) and a widow (mutawaffa 'anha). Note that the passage first gives the general rule then the evidence.
Divorced includes both revocable and irrevocable.
2
State the ruling for the divorced woman
The divorced woman must not leave the house day or night, except for necessity (house collapsing, danger) or if she commits an open obscenity (fahishah).
The exception of fahishah is disputed; we'll cover that in a separate lesson.
3
State the ruling for the widow
The widow may go out during the day and part of the night to seek a livelihood, but she must spend the night in the 'iddah house.
This is due to her lack of nafaqah (maintenance) from the husband.
4
Locate the proofs
The primary proof is Quran 65:1. For the widow, a hadith of Furai'ah is also cited to show that she may go out for needs.
5
Understand the rationale
The difference arises because the divorced woman receives nafaqah during 'iddah, but the widow does not; hence her need to work.
If the divorced woman's husband withholds nafaqah, some scholars allow her to go out; others do not.

رہنے کی ضرورت ہے اور چونکہ بسا اوقات کام کرتے کرتے رات آ جاتی ہے اور کچھ حصہ رات کا گذر بھی جاتا ہے۔ اسلئے دن کے ساتھ رات کے کچھ حصہ تک باہر رہنے کی اجازت دی گئی ہے۔ اور مطلقہ کا یہ حال نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ عدت کے زمانہ میں اس کا نفقہ شوہر کے مال میں واجب ہوگا۔ لہذا اس کو نکلنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ متوفی عنہا زوجہا کے جو از خروج کی تائید حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے۔
قال [؟] نلتى قتل زوجها هى فريعة قتل بنت مالک بن ابی سنان اخت ابی سعيد الخدري لما قتل زوجها جائت الى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم استاذنت ان تعتد في بني خدرة لا فى بيت زوجها فاذن لها رسول الله فلما خرجت دعاها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال لها اعيدى المسئلة فاعادت فقال لها لا حتى يبلغ الكتاب اجله يعنى لا تخرجی حتی تنقضی عدتک یعنی آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس عورت سے فرمایا جس کا شو ہر قتل کر دیا گیا تھا اور وہ فریعہ مالک بن ابی سنان کی بیٹی اور ابوسعید خدری کی بہن تھی۔ جب اس کا شوہر قتل کر دیا گیا تو وہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس آئی ( اور ) اس نے بنی خدرہ میں عدت گزارنے کی اجازت چاہی نہ کہ اپنے شوہر کے مکان میں ۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو اجازت دے دی۔ پس جب وہ نکل کر چلی تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو آواز دی اور فرمایا کہ مسئلہ کا اعادہ کرو ۔ اس نے مسئلہ دوبارہ بیان کیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا نہیں ۔ یہاں تک کہ عدت کا زمانہ ختم ہو جائے۔ یعنی اپنے شوہر کے مکان سے مت نکل ۔ یہاں تک کہ تیری عدت پوری ہو جائے۔ اس حدیث سے دو باتیں معلوم ہوئیں۔ ایک یہ کہ متوفی عنہا زوجہا پر شوہر کے مکان میں عدت گزارنا واجب ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ اپنی ضرورت پوری کرنے کیلئے نکلنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ عورت فتویٰ لینے کیلئے نکلی تھی ۔ مگر آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس پر نکیر نہیں فرمائی۔ آخر میں صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اگر کسی عورت نے اپنی عدت کے نفقہ پر ضلع کیا ۔ بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ طلب معاش کیلئے اس کو بھی دن میں نکلنے کی اجازت ہے اور بعض حضرات نے اجازت نہیں دی ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس عورت نے اپنا حق نفقہ وعدت بذات خود ساقط کیا ہے۔ لہذا اس پر جو شریعت کا حق واجب ہے۔ یعنی عدم خروج وہ باطل نہیں ہوگا۔ معتدہ پر لازم ہے کہ عدت اس مکان میں گزارے جس میں فرقت واقع ہوتے وقت رہائش تھی
وعلى المعتدة ان تعتد فى المنزل الذى يضاف اليها بالسكنى حال وقوع الفرقة والموت لقوله تعالى ولا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن والبيت المضاف اليها هو البيت الذى تسكنه ولهذا لو زارت اهلها وطلقها زوجها كان عليها ان تعود الى منزلها فتعتد فيه وقال عليه السلام للتي قتل زوجها اسکنى فى بيتك حتى يبلغ الكتاب اجله
ترجمہ اور معتدہ پر واجب ہے کہ اس مکان میں عدت گزارے، جو اس کی طرف رہنے کے ساتھ منسوب کیا جاتا ہے۔ جدائی اور موت کے وقت کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ولا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن - یعنی ان عورتوں کو ان کے گھروں سے مت نکالو اور ان کا گھر وہی ہے جس میں وہ رہتی تھیں۔ لہذا اگر وہ عورت اپنے میکے والوں کی زیارت کیلئے گئی ہو اور یہاں اس کے شوہر نے اس کو طلاق دے دی تو اس عورت پر واجب ہے کہ لوٹ کر اس گھر میں آئے اور اس میں عدت گزارے اور آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس عورت سے جس کا شو ہر شہید ہوا تھا یوں فرمایا کہ تو اپنے اس گھر میں ٹھہری رو یہاں تک کہ قرآن کے موافق مدت پوری ہو۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ معتدہ عورت شوہر کی وفات کے وقت اور فرقت واقع ہونے کے وقت جس مکان میں رہتی تھی اسی میں
Chapter of 'Iddah. She can go out during the day and part of the night, but she should not spend the night elsewhere than her house. In any case, for the divorced woman, the proof of this ruling is that Allah Almighty said: 'And do not expel them from their houses...' meaning, do not expel these women from the houses where they live, and they themselves should not go out, unless they commit an open obscenity (then it is another matter). Bayan al-Quran. And some said that 'fahishah' is the act of going out itself, and it was said that it is adultery, and they will be taken out for the execution of the hadd penalty. As for the woman whose husband has died, because she has no nafaqah, she needs to go out during the day to seek sustenance, and sometimes earning a livelihood extends until nightfall. The divorced woman is not like that, because nafaqah continues from her husband's wealth. So even if she was stingy regarding the nafaqah of her 'iddah, some scholars say she may go out during the day, and some say she may not, because she has nullified her own right. Therefore, that right will not become void because of it. Explanation of the issue: The woman who has been given a revocable or irrevocable divorce should not go out of the house in which she was living at the time of separation, night or day. Yes, if she is compelled to go out (e.g., fear of the house collapsing, or danger to her life or property, or the owner of the house kicks her out, e.g., she was living on rent and now cannot afford the rent), then there is no harm. For the woman whose husband has died, it is legally permitted to stay outside the house for the whole day and part of the night, provided she spends the night in her 'iddah house. She is not permitted to spend the night elsewhere. So for the divorced woman, the proof of not going out is the saying of Allah: 'Fear Allah, your Lord. Do not expel them from their houses, and they should not go out unless they commit an open obscenity.' That is, fear Allah who is your Lord. Do not expel these women from their houses (because the right of lodging for a divorced woman is obligatory like a wife), and they themselves should not go out unless they commit an open obscenity, then it is another matter. For example, if they commit adultery or theft, they should be taken out for punishment. Or according to some scholars, if they talk harshly and constantly cause distress and quarrels, it is permissible to expel them. (Bayan al-Quran) There is a difference among scholars regarding the interpretation of the word 'fahishah'. Some scholars are of the opinion that 'fahishah' means the act of going out itself. This is the saying of Ibrahim al-Makhfi, and Imam A'zam Abu Hanifa selected it. In this case, the meaning of the verse would be that the women in 'iddah should not go out from their houses unless their going out is itself a 'fahishah', i.e., an obscene act. This is like it is said: 'No one abuses the Prophet, peace be upon him, except a disbeliever, and no one commits adultery except a sinful person.' And some scholars are of the opinion that 'fahishah' means adultery. Then the meaning would be that the women in 'iddah should not go out. Yes, if they have committed adultery, they will be taken out to execute the hadd penalty. This is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud, and Imam Abu Yusuf selected it. And Ibn Abbas said that 'fahishah' means the woman being rebellious and disobedient. And for the woman whose husband has died, the proof of permission to go out during the day and part of the night is that the woman whose husband has died has no nafaqah. Therefore, she needs to stay outside for earning a livelihood, and since sometimes working extends until nightfall and part of the night passes, she is permitted to stay outside for a part of the night along with the day. The divorced woman is not like this, because during the period of 'iddah, her nafaqah is obligatory from her husband's wealth. Hence, she has no need to go out. The permissibility of going out for the woman whose husband has died is also supported by a hadith. He said: [Hadith of Furai'ah...] meaning the Prophet peace be upon him said to the woman whose husband was killed, and she was Furai'ah bint Malik bin Abi Sinan, the sister of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. When her husband was killed, she came to the Messenger of Allah and asked permission to spend her 'iddah in Bani Khidrah, not in her husband's house. The Messenger of Allah gave her permission. Then when she left, the Messenger of Allah called her and said, 'Repeat the question.' So she repeated it, and he said, 'No, until the book reaches its term,' meaning, do not go out until your 'iddah is complete. From this hadith, two things are learned: first, that it is obligatory for the woman whose husband has died to spend 'iddah in her husband's house; second, that it is permissible to go out to fulfill a need, because this woman had gone out to seek a fatwa, but the Prophet did not disapprove of her. At the end, the author of Hidayah said: If a woman is stingy regarding the nafaqah of her 'iddah, some scholars are of the opinion that she is also permitted to go out during the day to seek maintenance, and some have not allowed it. Their proof is that this woman has herself nullified her right to nafaqah and 'iddah. Therefore, the right of Shari'ah that is obligatory upon her, i.e., not going out, will not become void. It is obligatory upon a woman in 'iddah to spend her 'iddah in the house in which she was residing at the time of separation. And the woman in 'iddah must observe 'iddah in the house that is attributed to her by residence at the time of separation and death, because of the saying of Allah: 'Do not expel them from their houses.' And the house attributed to her is the house she lives in. Therefore, if she visited her family and her husband divorced her, she must return to her house and observe 'iddah in it. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to the woman whose husband was killed: 'Stay in your house until the book reaches its term.' Translation: And it is obligatory upon the woman in 'iddah to spend 'iddah in that house which is attributed to her by residence at the time of separation and death, because Allah said 'Do not expel them from their houses' - that is, do not expel these women from their houses, and their house is the one in which they were living. Therefore, if a woman went to visit her family and her husband divorced her there, it is obligatory upon her to return to that house and spend her 'iddah in it. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to the woman whose husband was martyred: 'Stay in your house until the period according to the Quran is completed.' Explanation of the issue: The woman in 'iddah should observe 'iddah in the same house in which she was living at the time of the husband's death or divorce.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Hidayah discusses the rules of 'iddah regarding the residence of the woman. It begins by distinguishing between a divorced woman (muttalaqah) and a widow (mutawaffa 'anha zuhha). For a divorced woman (whether revocable or irrevocable), she is generally prohibited from leaving the house day or night, with the exception if she commits an 'open obscenity' (fahishah mubayyinah). The Quranic verse (At-Talaq 65:1) is cited as proof: 'Do not expel them from their houses, and they should not go out, unless they commit an open obscenity.' There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the interpretation of fahishah: Imam Abu Hanifa (following Ibrahim al-Makhfi) interprets it as the act of going out itself, meaning that if she leaves without necessity, that act becomes the fahishah, so expulsion is not permitted for any other reason. Imam Abu Yusuf (following Ibn Mas'ud) interprets it as zina (adultery), so she may only be expelled for that offense. Ibn Abbas interprets it as nushuz (rebellion). The text also mentions that if the woman is compelled to leave due to danger or eviction, she may go out.

For a widow, the rule is different because she has no nafaqah. She is permitted to go out during the day and part of the night to seek a livelihood, but she must return to her house by night. This is supported by the hadith of Furai'ah bint Malik, which shows that a widow must observe 'iddah in her husband's house but may go out for necessities (like seeking a fatwa). The hadith also establishes the obligation of staying in the husband's house for 'iddah.

The passage then discusses a scenario where the husband withholds nafaqah during 'iddah: some scholars permit her to go out during the day to earn, while others prohibit it because she has voluntarily waived her right to nafaqah, but the Shari'ah right of staying in the house remains.

Finally, the general principle is stated: The woman must observe 'iddah in the house where she was residing at the time of separation or death. If she was away visiting family and divorce occurred, she must return to the marital home. This is derived from the Quran and the hadith of Furai'ah.

Key Terms
عدت ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before she can remarry.
فاحشة (fahishah): An open obscenity or immoral act. In this context, it is the condition that permits expelling a woman from her 'iddah house.
مطلقہ (muttalaqah): A woman who has been divorced by her husband.
متوفی عنہا زوجہا (mutawaffa 'anha zujhuha): A woman whose husband has died, i.e., a widow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is TRUE regarding a widow's 'iddah?
A) She must remain in her house 24 hours a day for four months and ten days.
B) She may go out during the day and part of the night to seek a livelihood, but must return home by night.
C) She may leave the house only if she commits a fahishah.
D) She may live anywhere she chooses during 'iddah.

Key Takeaway
A divorced woman must stay home day and night; a widow may work during the day but must return for the night.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
The Interpretation of 'Fahishah' in 'Iddah: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf
Explains the intra-Hanafi dispute on interpretation of fahishah in Quran 65:1

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi interpretations of 'fahishah' in Quran 65:1 and identify the practical difference (thamarah) between them.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: fahishah is the act of going out itself; Abu Yusuf: it is zina. This affects when a woman may be expelled from her 'iddah house.

The Quranic exception of 'fahishah mubayyinah' in the 'iddah verse has been understood differently by the great Hanafi imams. This intra-madhhab dispute has a real impact on when a divorced woman may be expelled. In this lesson, we will dissect the two positions, their proofs, and their consequences.

Guided Path
1
Locate the dispute in the passage
The passage explicitly mentions a difference among scholars regarding the word 'fahishah' in Surah At-Talaq 65:1.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa, following Ibrahim al-Makhfi, holds that 'fahishah' means the act of going out itself. Thus, a woman may only be expelled if her going out is itself an obscene act (i.e., leaving without a valid reason is fahishah).
This implies she cannot be expelled for any other reason; expulsion is not permitted unless she leaves.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf, following Ibn Mas'ud, holds that 'fahishah' means zina (adultery). Therefore, she may be expelled only if she commits adultery, for the purpose of executing the hadd penalty.
This narrows the exception to a specific grave sin.
4
Identify the thamarah (practical difference)
Under Abu Hanifa, a woman who stays home cannot be expelled; if she goes out without necessity, her act is the fahishah. Under Abu Yusuf, even if she goes out, she cannot be expelled unless she commits zina. This affects what triggers the right to expel.
Both agree that staying home is the norm; the dispute is about the exception.
5
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa relies on a linguistic analysis that considers the word 'fahishah' to be the act of going out, based on istihsan. Abu Yusuf relies on the common usage of 'fahishah' for zina and a hadith (not quoted in passage). Ibn Abbas adds a third view: nushuz.
The commentator does not give tarjih, but Hidayah often favors Abu Hanifa.
