ہوں تو ان کو نکال دینا جائز ہے۔ (بیان القرآن ) لفظ فاحشہ کی تفسیر میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے۔ بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ فاحشہ سے مراد نفس خروج ہے۔ یہ قول ابراہیم مخفی کا ہے اور اسی کو اختیار کیا ہے امام اعظم ابو حنیفہ نے۔ اس صورت میں آیت کے معنی ہوں گے کہ معتدہ عورتیں اپنے گھروں سے نہ نکلیں مگر یہ کہ ان کا نکلنا فاحشہ یعنی بے حیائی کی بات ہوگی۔ یہ ایسا ہے جیسے کہا جاتا ہے لا يسب النبی عليه السلام الا كافر ولا يزنى احد الا ان يكون فاسقاً یعنی نبی علیہ السلام کو گالی دینا کفر ہے اور زنا کر نا فسق ہے اور بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ فاحشہ سے مراد زنا ہے۔ اب مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ معتدہ عورتیں نہ نکلیں ۔ ہاں اگر انہوں نے زنا کا ارتکاب کیا ہو تو حد جاری کرنے کیلئے ان کو نکالا جائے گا۔ یہ قول ہے ابن مسعود کا اور اس کو اختیار کیا ہے امام ابو یوسف نے اور ابن عباس نے فرمایا کہ فاحشہ سے مراد عورت کا ناشزہ اور نا فرمان ہونا ہے۔ اور متوفی عنہا زوجہا کے دن بھر اور رات کے کچھ حصہ گھر سے باہر رہنے کی اجازت پر دلیل یہ ہے کہ متوفی عنہا زوجہا کے واسطے نفقہ نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اس کو طلب معاش کیلئے گھر سے باہر رہنے کی ضرورت ہے اور چونکہ بسا اوقات کام کرتے کرتے رات آ جاتی ہے اور کچھ حصہ رات کا گذر بھی جاتا ہے۔ اسلئے دن کے ساتھ رات کے کچھ حصہ تک باہر رہنے کی اجازت دی گئی ہے۔ اور مطلقہ کا یہ حال نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ عدت کے زمانہ میں اس کا نفقہ شوہر کے مال میں واجب ہوگا۔ لہذا اس کو نکلنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ متوفی عنہا زوجہا کے جو از خروج کی تائید حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے۔
قال [؟] نلتى قتل زوجها هى فريعة قتل بنت مالک بن ابی سنان اخت ابی سعيد الخدري لما قتل زوجها جائت الى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم استاذنت ان تعتد في بني خدرة لا فى بيت زوجها فاذن لها رسول الله فلما خرجت دعاها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال لها اعيدى المسئلة فاعادت فقال لها لا حتى يبلغ الكتاب اجله يعنى لا تخرجی حتی تنقضی عدتک یعنی آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس عورت سے فرمایا جس کا شو ہر قتل کر دیا گیا تھا اور وہ فریعہ مالک بن ابی سنان کی بیٹی اور ابوسعید خدری کی بہن تھی۔ جب اس کا شوہر قتل کر دیا گیا تو وہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس آئی ( اور ) اس نے بنی خدرہ میں عدت گزارنے کی اجازت چاہی نہ کہ اپنے شوہر کے مکان میں ۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو اجازت دے دی۔ پس جب وہ نکل کر چلی تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو آواز دی اور فرمایا کہ مسئلہ کا اعادہ کرو ۔ اس نے مسئلہ دوبارہ بیان کیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا نہیں ۔ یہاں تک کہ عدت کا زمانہ ختم ہو جائے۔ یعنی اپنے شوہر کے مکان سے مت نکل ۔ یہاں تک کہ تیری عدت پوری ہو جائے۔ اس حدیث سے دو باتیں معلوم ہوئیں۔ ایک یہ کہ متوفی عنہا زوجہا پر شوہر کے مکان میں عدت گزارنا واجب ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ اپنی ضرورت پوری کرنے کیلئے نکلنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ عورت فتویٰ لینے کیلئے نکلی تھی ۔ مگر آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس پر نکیر نہیں فرمائی۔ آخر میں صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اگر کسی عورت نے اپنی عدت کے نفقہ پر ضلع کیا ۔ بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ طلب معاش کیلئے اس کو بھی دن میں نکلنے کی اجازت ہے اور بعض حضرات نے اجازت نہیں دی ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس عورت نے اپنا حق نفقہ وعدت بذات خود ساقط کیا ہے۔ لہذا اس پر جو شریعت کا حق واجب ہے۔ یعنی عدم خروج وہ باطل نہیں ہوگا۔ معتدہ پر لازم ہے کہ عدت اس مکان میں گزارے جس میں فرقت واقع ہوتے وقت رہائش تھی
وعلى المعتدة ان تعتد فى المنزل الذى يضاف اليها بالسكنى حال وقوع الفرقة والموت لقوله تعالى ولا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن والبيت المضاف اليها هو البيت الذى تسكنه ولهذا لو زارت اهلها وطلقها زوجها كان عليها ان تعود الى منزلها فتعتد فيه وقال عليه السلام للتي قتل زوجها اسکنى فى بيتك حتى يبلغ الكتاب اجله
ترجمہ اور معتدہ پر واجب ہے کہ اس مکان میں عدت گزارے، جو اس کی طرف رہنے کے ساتھ منسوب کیا جاتا ہے۔ جدائی اور موت کے وقت کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ولا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن - یعنی ان عورتوں کو ان کے گھروں سے مت نکالو اور ان کا گھر وہی ہے جس میں وہ رہتی تھیں۔ لہذا اگر وہ عورت اپنے میکے والوں کی زیارت کیلئے گئی ہو اور یہاں اس کے شوہر نے اس کو طلاق دے دی تو اس عورت پر واجب ہے کہ لوٹ کر اس گھر میں آئے اور اس میں عدت گزارے اور آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس عورت سے جس کا شو ہر شہید ہوا تھا یوں فرمایا کہ تو اپنے اس گھر میں ٹھہری رو یہاں تک کہ قرآن کے موافق مدت پوری ہو۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ معتدہ عورت شوہر کی وفات کے وقت اور فرقت واقع ہونے کے وقت جس مکان میں رہتی تھی اسی میں
Chapter of 'Iddah. She can go out during the day and part of the night, but she should not spend the night elsewhere than her house. In any case, for the divorced woman, the proof of this ruling is that Allah Almighty said: 'And do not expel them from their houses...' meaning, do not expel these women from the houses where they live, and they themselves should not go out, unless they commit an open obscenity (then it is another matter). Bayan al-Quran. And some said that 'fahishah' is the act of going out itself, and it was said that it is adultery, and they will be taken out for the execution of the hadd penalty. As for the woman whose husband has died, because she has no nafaqah, she needs to go out during the day to seek sustenance, and sometimes earning a livelihood extends until nightfall. The divorced woman is not like that, because nafaqah continues from her husband's wealth. So even if she was stingy regarding the nafaqah of her 'iddah, some scholars say she may go out during the day, and some say she may not, because she has nullified her own right. Therefore, that right will not become void because of it. Explanation of the issue: The woman who has been given a revocable or irrevocable divorce should not go out of the house in which she was living at the time of separation, night or day. Yes, if she is compelled to go out (e.g., fear of the house collapsing, or danger to her life or property, or the owner of the house kicks her out, e.g., she was living on rent and now cannot afford the rent), then there is no harm. For the woman whose husband has died, it is legally permitted to stay outside the house for the whole day and part of the night, provided she spends the night in her 'iddah house. She is not permitted to spend the night elsewhere. So for the divorced woman, the proof of not going out is the saying of Allah: 'Fear Allah, your Lord. Do not expel them from their houses, and they should not go out unless they commit an open obscenity.' That is, fear Allah who is your Lord. Do not expel these women from their houses (because the right of lodging for a divorced woman is obligatory like a wife), and they themselves should not go out unless they commit an open obscenity, then it is another matter. For example, if they commit adultery or theft, they should be taken out for punishment. Or according to some scholars, if they talk harshly and constantly cause distress and quarrels, it is permissible to expel them. (Bayan al-Quran) There is a difference among scholars regarding the interpretation of the word 'fahishah'. Some scholars are of the opinion that 'fahishah' means the act of going out itself. This is the saying of Ibrahim al-Makhfi, and Imam A'zam Abu Hanifa selected it. In this case, the meaning of the verse would be that the women in 'iddah should not go out from their houses unless their going out is itself a 'fahishah', i.e., an obscene act. This is like it is said: 'No one abuses the Prophet, peace be upon him, except a disbeliever, and no one commits adultery except a sinful person.' And some scholars are of the opinion that 'fahishah' means adultery. Then the meaning would be that the women in 'iddah should not go out. Yes, if they have committed adultery, they will be taken out to execute the hadd penalty. This is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud, and Imam Abu Yusuf selected it. And Ibn Abbas said that 'fahishah' means the woman being rebellious and disobedient. And for the woman whose husband has died, the proof of permission to go out during the day and part of the night is that the woman whose husband has died has no nafaqah. Therefore, she needs to stay outside for earning a livelihood, and since sometimes working extends until nightfall and part of the night passes, she is permitted to stay outside for a part of the night along with the day. The divorced woman is not like this, because during the period of 'iddah, her nafaqah is obligatory from her husband's wealth. Hence, she has no need to go out. The permissibility of going out for the woman whose husband has died is also supported by a hadith. He said: [Hadith of Furai'ah...] meaning the Prophet peace be upon him said to the woman whose husband was killed, and she was Furai'ah bint Malik bin Abi Sinan, the sister of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. When her husband was killed, she came to the Messenger of Allah and asked permission to spend her 'iddah in Bani Khidrah, not in her husband's house. The Messenger of Allah gave her permission. Then when she left, the Messenger of Allah called her and said, 'Repeat the question.' So she repeated it, and he said, 'No, until the book reaches its term,' meaning, do not go out until your 'iddah is complete. From this hadith, two things are learned: first, that it is obligatory for the woman whose husband has died to spend 'iddah in her husband's house; second, that it is permissible to go out to fulfill a need, because this woman had gone out to seek a fatwa, but the Prophet did not disapprove of her. At the end, the author of Hidayah said: If a woman is stingy regarding the nafaqah of her 'iddah, some scholars are of the opinion that she is also permitted to go out during the day to seek maintenance, and some have not allowed it. Their proof is that this woman has herself nullified her right to nafaqah and 'iddah. Therefore, the right of Shari'ah that is obligatory upon her, i.e., not going out, will not become void. It is obligatory upon a woman in 'iddah to spend her 'iddah in the house in which she was residing at the time of separation. And the woman in 'iddah must observe 'iddah in the house that is attributed to her by residence at the time of separation and death, because of the saying of Allah: 'Do not expel them from their houses.' And the house attributed to her is the house she lives in. Therefore, if she visited her family and her husband divorced her, she must return to her house and observe 'iddah in it. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to the woman whose husband was killed: 'Stay in your house until the book reaches its term.' Translation: And it is obligatory upon the woman in 'iddah to spend 'iddah in that house which is attributed to her by residence at the time of separation and death, because Allah said 'Do not expel them from their houses' - that is, do not expel these women from their houses, and their house is the one in which they were living. Therefore, if a woman went to visit her family and her husband divorced her there, it is obligatory upon her to return to that house and spend her 'iddah in it. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to the woman whose husband was martyred: 'Stay in your house until the period according to the Quran is completed.' Explanation of the issue: The woman in 'iddah should observe 'iddah in the same house in which she was living at the time of the husband's death or divorce.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Hidayah discusses the rules of 'iddah regarding the residence of the woman. It begins by distinguishing between a divorced woman (muttalaqah) and a widow (mutawaffa 'anha zuhha). For a divorced woman (whether revocable or irrevocable), she is generally prohibited from leaving the house day or night, with the exception if she commits an 'open obscenity' (fahishah mubayyinah). The Quranic verse (At-Talaq 65:1) is cited as proof: 'Do not expel them from their houses, and they should not go out, unless they commit an open obscenity.' There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the interpretation of fahishah: Imam Abu Hanifa (following Ibrahim al-Makhfi) interprets it as the act of going out itself, meaning that if she leaves without necessity, that act becomes the fahishah, so expulsion is not permitted for any other reason. Imam Abu Yusuf (following Ibn Mas'ud) interprets it as zina (adultery), so she may only be expelled for that offense. Ibn Abbas interprets it as nushuz (rebellion). The text also mentions that if the woman is compelled to leave due to danger or eviction, she may go out.

For a widow, the rule is different because she has no nafaqah. She is permitted to go out during the day and part of the night to seek a livelihood, but she must return to her house by night. This is supported by the hadith of Furai'ah bint Malik, which shows that a widow must observe 'iddah in her husband's house but may go out for necessities (like seeking a fatwa). The hadith also establishes the obligation of staying in the husband's house for 'iddah.

The passage then discusses a scenario where the husband withholds nafaqah during 'iddah: some scholars permit her to go out during the day to earn, while others prohibit it because she has voluntarily waived her right to nafaqah, but the Shari'ah right of staying in the house remains.

Finally, the general principle is stated: The woman must observe 'iddah in the house where she was residing at the time of separation or death. If she was away visiting family and divorce occurred, she must return to the marital home. This is derived from the Quran and the hadith of Furai'ah.

Key Terms
فاحشة (fahishah): An open obscenity or immoral act. In this context, the key disputed term in Quran 65:1.
خروج (khuruj): The act of going out or leaving the house.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what does 'fahishah' mean in the context of 'iddah?
A) Adultery (zina)
B) The act of going out of the house without necessity
C) Theft
D) Disobedience (nushuz)

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of 'fahishah' differs between Abu Hanifa (act of leaving) and Abu Yusuf (zina), affecting when a woman may be expelled from her 'iddah house.

Module 2 · Lesson 311

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Obligation of iddah in the marital home and exceptions
Ruling with proof on iddah residence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where a woman must observe iddah, identify the Quranic and hadith proofs, and apply the exceptions for excused relocation.

Core Idea
A woman in iddah must stay in the marital home; leaving is only permitted for a genuine need or if staying causes hardship.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes the core ruling that a woman observing iddah (post-divorce or widowhood) must remain in the house where she resided at the time of separation. The proof is drawn from the Quranic command 'Do not expel them from their houses' and the Prophet's ﷺ instruction to a widow to stay in her house until the iddah ends. However, the passage also acknowledges exceptions: if the woman's share of the house is insufficient and heirs expel her, or if she fears for her belongings or safety, she may move to another house. This lesson will walk you through the evidence, the definition of 'house,' and the circumstances that allow relocation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine which specific act is being ruled upon and the level of obligation (hukm level). The act is: a woman in iddah staying in the marital home. The Hanafi ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory).
Wajib not fard because evidence is zanni al-thubut (ahad hadith) and the Quranic imperative is interpreted as a prohibition of expulsion, not a direct command to stay.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The passage cites two proofs: Quran 65:1 'Do not expel them from their houses' and the hadith of Fari'ah bint Malik where the Prophet commanded a widow to stay in her house until the iddah ends. Understand how each proof leads to the obligation.
The hadith also shows permission to leave for necessity (she went to seek a fatwa) – this establishes the principle that leaving for a valid need is allowed.
3
Understand the definition of 'house' (bayt) and 'residence' (sukna)
The passage states that 'house' refers to the dwelling where she lived at the time of separation, regardless of whether she owned, borrowed, or rented it. This broad definition ensures stability for the woman.
Important: if she was visiting her family and divorce occurred, she must return to the marital home.
4
Recognize exceptions for excused relocation
The passage lists specific excuses that permit moving: (1) insufficient share in the inherited house + heirs expelling her, (2) fear for belongings, (3) fear of house collapse, (4) inability to pay rent. These are based on qiyas and the precedent of Ali (RA) moving Umm Kulthum after Umar's (RA) death.
The principle: 'Acts of worship are affected by excuses' – hardship lightens the obligation.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on disputing maintenance
The passage mentions a difference of opinion when a woman disputes her nafaqah (maintenance): some Hanafi scholars allow her to go out during the day to earn, others forbid it because she waived her right. The mufta bihi is that she must stay unless a valid excuse exists.
This shows how usul principles (waiving a right does not waive a Shari'ah obligation) are applied.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد نهم
اور مطلقہ کا یہ حال نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ عدت کے زمانہ میں اس کا نفقہ شوہر کے مال میں واجب ہوگا۔ لہذا اس کو نکلنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ متوفی عنہاز و جہا کے جو از خروج کی تائید حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے۔
قال نلتى قتل زوجها هى فريعة قتل بنت مالک بن ابی سنان اخت ابی سعيد الخدري لما قتل زوجها جائت الى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم استاذنت ان تعتد في بني خدرة لا فى بيت زوجها فاذن لها رسول الله فلما خرجت دعاها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال لها اعيدى المسئلة فاعادت فقال لها لا حتى يبلغ الكتاب اجله يعنى لا تخرجی حتی تنقضی عدتک یعنی آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس عورت سے فرمایا جس کا شو ہر قتل کر دیا گیا تھا اور وہ فریعہ مالک بن ابی سنان کی بیٹی اور ابوسعید خدری کی بہن تھی۔ جب اس کا شوہر قتل کر دیا گیا تو وہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس آئی ( اور ) اس نے بنی خدرہ میں عدت گزارنے کی اجازت چاہی نہ کہ اپنے شوہر کے مکان میں ۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو اجازت دے دی۔ پس جب وہ نکل کر چلی تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو آواز دی اور فرمایا کہ مسئلہ کا اعادہ کرو ۔ اس نے مسئلہ دوبارہ بیان کیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا نہیں ۔ یہاں تک کہ عدت کا زمانہ ختم ہو جائے۔ یعنی اپنے شوہر کے مکان سے مت نکل ۔ یہاں تک کہ تیری عدت پوری ہو جائے۔ اس حدیث سے دو باتیں معلوم ہوئیں۔ ایک یہ کہ متوفی عنہا زوجہا پر شوہر کے مکان میں عدت گزارنا واجب ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ اپنی ضرورت پوری کرنے کیلئے نکلنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ عورت فتویٰ لینے کیلئے نکلی تھی ۔ مگر آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس پر نکیر نہیں فرمائی۔ آخر میں صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اگر کسی عورت نے اپنی عدت کے نفقہ پر ضلع کیا ۔ بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ طلب معاش کیلئے اس کو بھی دن میں نکلنے کی اجازت ہے اور بعض حضرات نے اجازت نہیں دی ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس عورت نے اپنا حق نفقہ وعدت ) بذات خود ساقط کیا ہے۔ لہذا اس پر جو شریعت کا حق واجب ہے۔ یعنی عدم خروج وہ باطل نہیں ہوگا۔ معتدہ پر لازم ہے کہ عدت اس مکان میں گزارے جس میں فرقت واقع ہوتے وقت رہائش تھی
وعلى المعتدة ان تعتد فى المنزل الذى يضاف اليها بالسكنى حال وقوع الفرقة والموت لقوله تعالى ولا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن والبيت المضاف اليها هو البيت الذى تسكنه ولهذا لوزارت اهلها وطلقها زوجها كان عليها ان تعود الى منزلها فتعتد فيه وقال عليه السلام للتي قتل زوجها اسکنى فى بيتك حتى يبلغ الكتاب اجله
ترجمہ اور معتدہ پر واجب ہے کہ اس مکان میں عدت گزارے، جو اس کی طرف رہنے کے ساتھ منسوب کیا جاتا ہے۔ جدائی اور موت کے وقت کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ولا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن - یعنی ان عورتوں کو ان کے گھروں سے مت نکالو اور ان کا گھر وہی ہے جس میں وہ رہتی تھیں۔ لہذا اگر وہ عورت اپنے میکے والوں کی زیارت کیلئے گئی ہو اور یہاں اس کے شوہر نے اس کو طلاق دے دی تو اس عورت پر واجب ہے کہ لوٹ کر اس گھر میں آئے اور اس میں عدت گزارے اور آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس عورت سے جس کا شو ہر شہید ہوا تھا یوں فرمایا کہ تو اپنے اس گھر میں ٹھہری رو یہاں تک کہ قرآن کے موافق مدت پوری ہو۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ معتدہ عورت شوہر کی وفات کے وقت اور فرقت واقع ہونے کے وقت جس مکان میں رہتی تھی اسی میں

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
۱۹۳
باب العدة
عدت گذار نا واجب ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے و لا تخرجوهن من بیوتھن اور عورت کا بیت وہ کہلائے گا جس میں وہ رہتی تھی۔
اور ور سکنی یعنی رہنا عام ہے بطریق ملک رہتی ہو یا بطریق استعارہ یا بطریق استاجر ہ ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر عورت اپنے میکے گئی ہوئی تھی ۔ پس شوہر نے وہیں رہتے ہوئے اس کو طلاق دے دی تو اس عورت پر واجب ہے کہ یہ لوٹ کر اپنے اسی گھر میں عدت گزارے جس میں یہ رہتی تھی۔
اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس عورت سے جس کا شو ہر شہید ہوا تھایوں فرمایا کہ تو اپنے اس گھر میں ٹھہری رہ ۔ یہاں تک کہ اللہ تعالی کے فرمان کے مطابق تیری عدت پوری ہو جائے۔
اگر شوہر کے گھر سے اس عورت کا حصہ اس کیلئے نا کافی ہو اور ورثہ اس کو اپنے حصے سے نکال دیں تو عورت منتقل ہو جائے
و ان كان نصيبها من دار الميت لا يكفيها فاخرجها لورثة من نصيبهم انتقلت لأن هذا انتقال بعذر و العبادات توثر فيها الاعذار وصار كما اذا خافت على متاعها او خافت سقوط المنزل او كانت فيها باجر ولا تجد ما تؤديه ترجمہ اور اگر شوہر متوفی کے گھر میں سے اس عورت کا حصہ اس کے واسطے نا کافی ہو اور ورثہ اس کو اپنے حصہ سے نکال دیں تو یہ عورت منتقل ہو جائے ۔ کیونکہ ( یہ ) منتقل ہونا عذر کی وجہ سے ہے اور عبادات میں اعذار مؤثر ہوتے ہیں اور ( یہ ) ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ عورت کو اپنے سامان کا خوف ہوایا گھر کے گرنے کا خوف ہوا۔ یا اس گھر میں کرایہ پر رہتی تھی اور اب وہ کرایہ ادا نہیں کر سکتی ۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر متوفی کے مکان میں سے عورت کا حصہ اتنا نا کافی ہے کہ وہ اس میں نہیں رہ سکتی اور دوسرے ورثہ نے بھی اپنے حصتہ میں رہنے کی اجازت نہیں دی۔ تو ایسی صورت میں یہ عورت دوسرے کسی مکان میں منتقل ہو سکتی ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اسن کا منتقل ہونا عذر کی وجہ سے ہے اور عبادات میں عذر معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے یہاں بھی عذر معتبر ہوگا اور اس پر ایک دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت عمر کی شہادت کے بعد حضرت علی نے اپنی صاحبزادی ام کلثوم کو بیت العدت سے منتقل فرمایا۔ کیونکہ حضرت عمر خلیفہ ہونے کی وجہ سے سرکاری مکان میں سکونت پذیر تھے اور آپ کی شہادت کے بعد یہ مکان تیسرے خلیفہ حضرت عثمان غنی کے استعمال میں آ گیا۔ اس وجہ سے ام کلثوم ( زوجہ عمر ) کو اس مکان سے منتقل کرنے کی ضرورت پیش آئی۔ عینی شرح ہدایہ ) (
اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ عورت کو اس بات کا خوف ہو کہ میرا سامان چور اٹھالے جائیں گے۔ یا مکان گرنے کا ڈر ہو۔ یا یہ کہ اس مکان میں کرایہ پر تھی اور اب کرایہ ادا کرنے کی گنجائش نہیں رہی۔ تو جس طرح ان صورتوں میں معتدہ وفات کو منتقل ہونے کی اجازت ہے۔ اسی طرح مذکورہ بالا صورت میں بھی منتقل ہونے کی اجازت ہے۔
اگر فرقت طلاق بائن یا تین طلاقوں سے واقع ہوئی ہو تو دونوں کے درمیان سترہ ہونا ضروری ہے
ثم ان وقعت لفرقة بطلاق بائن اوثلث لابد من سترة بينهما ثم لاباس لانه معترف بالحرمة الا ان يكون فاسقا يخاف عليها منه فحينئذ تخرج لانه عذر ولا تخرج عما انتقلت اليه والاولى ان يخرج هو ويتركها
Chapter of Iddah. And the divorced woman is not like this. Because during the iddah her maintenance is obligatory from the husband's wealth, so she has no need to go out. For the widow, permission to go out is also supported by hadith. He said: Umm Fari'ah bint Malik bin Abi Sinan, sister of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, when her husband was killed, she came to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and asked permission to observe her iddah in Banu Khidrah, not in her husband's house. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, permitted her. When she went out, he called her and said: Repeat the question. She repeated it, and he said: No, until the appointed term is reached. i.e., do not go out until your iddah is completed. From this hadith two things are learned: First, that it is obligatory for a widow to observe iddah in her husband's house. Second, that going out for a need is permissible, because this woman went out to seek a fatwa, and the Prophet did not rebuke her. At the end, the author of al-Hidayah said: If a woman disputes about her iddah maintenance, some scholars opine that she may go out during the day to earn a living, while others do not permit it. Their proof is that she has dropped her own right to maintenance, so the obligation of Shari'ah upon her, i.e., not going out, is not invalidated. It is obligatory upon the woman in iddah to observe iddah in the house in which she was residing at the time of separation and death. It is obligatory upon the woman in iddah to observe iddah in the house which is attributed to her by residence at the time of separation and death, because Allah Most High said: 'Do not expel them from their houses.' And her house is the house in which she lives. Therefore, if she had gone to her family and her husband divorced her, she must return to her house and observe iddah there. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to the woman whose husband was killed: 'Stay in your house until the appointed term is reached.' Explanation of the issue: A woman in iddah must observe iddah in the house in which she was living at the time of her husband's death or separation. The proof is that Allah said: 'Do not expel them from their houses,' and a woman's house is called that in which she lived. And residence is general, whether she lived by ownership, by borrowing, or by rent. This is why if a woman had gone to her family and her husband divorced her while she was there, she must return to her house and observe iddah there. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to the woman whose husband was martyred: 'Stay in your house until your iddah is completed according to Allah's command.' If the woman's share in the deceased husband's house is insufficient for her and the heirs expel her from their shares, she may move, because this moving is due to an excuse, and excuses affect acts of worship. It becomes like when she fears for her belongings, or fears the house collapsing, or she was living there for rent and cannot pay. Explanation of the scenario: If the woman's share in the deceased husband's house is insufficient such that she cannot live in it, and the other heirs do not permit her to live in their shares, then in such a case she may move to another house. The proof is that her moving is due to an excuse, and excuses are considered in acts of worship. For this reason, the excuse will be considered here. Another proof is that after Umar's martyrdom, Ali moved his daughter Umm Kulthum from the house of iddah, because Umar, being Caliph, was residing in a government house, and after his martyrdom that house came into use for the third Caliph Uthman Ghani. Thus there was need to move Umm Kulthum (Umar's wife) from that house. (Ayni, Sharh al-Hidayah). And this is like when a woman fears that her goods might be stolen, or fears the house collapsing, or she was in the house on rent and cannot pay. Just as in these cases the widow is allowed to move, likewise in the mentioned case she is allowed to move. If separation occurs by irrevocable divorce or three divorces, a screen between them is necessary. Then if the separation occurs by irrevocable divorce or three, a screen between them is necessary; then there is no harm because he acknowledges the prohibition. Unless he is a transgressor who may be feared for her; then she may go out because of the excuse, but she should not leave the place she moved to. It is better that he goes out and leaves her.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof concerning the obligation of a woman in iddah (waiting period) to remain in the marital home. The passage begins by distinguishing between a divorced woman and a widow: a divorced woman's maintenance is obligatory, so she does not need to go out. For a widow, the hadith of Fari'ah bint Malik is presented as proof. In this hadith, the Prophet initially permitted her to observe iddah elsewhere, but then called her back and forbade it, commanding her to stay in her own house until the iddah ends. From this, two rulings are derived: (1) It is wajib (obligatory) for a widow to observe iddah in her husband's house. (2) It is permissible to leave for a genuine need, as the woman went out to seek a fatwa and the Prophet did not reproach her. The author of al-Hidayah then notes a difference of opinion regarding a woman who disputes about her maintenance: some scholars allow her to go out during the day to earn a living, while others disallow it because she has waived her right, so the Shari'ah obligation of staying remains. The passage then shifts to the core ruling: a woman must observe iddah in the house where she was residing at the time of separation (death or divorce). The Quranic verse 'Do not expel them from their houses' is cited, and the term 'house' is defined as the dwelling where she lived, regardless of whether she owned, borrowed, or rented it. If she was visiting her family and divorce occurred, she must return to her marital home. Exceptions are then provided based on necessity: if her share of the inherited house is insufficient and the heirs expel her, she may move to another house. This is qiyas on other acceptable excuses, such as fear for her belongings, fear of the house collapsing, or inability to pay rent. Historical precedent is given: after Umar's martyrdom, Ali moved Umm Kulthum because the government house was needed for the next caliph. Finally, if the separation is by irrevocable divorce (ba'in) or three divorces, a physical screen between the former spouses is required; if the husband is a fasiq feared to harm her, she may leave, but it is better for the husband to depart.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): The legally prescribed waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband, during which she cannot remarry.
معتدہ (mu'taddah): A woman currently observing iddah.
بیت (bayt): The house where the woman resided at the time of separation, regardless of ownership or rental status.
سکنی (sukna): Residence or living arrangement; the right to dwell in a place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Fari'ah, what is the consequence of a widow leaving the house for a valid need?
A) It is prohibited and invalidates the iddah.
B) It is permissible, as the Prophet did not rebuke her.
C) It is makruh but iddah is valid.
D) It requires a compensatory fast.

Key Takeaway
A woman in iddah must stay in the marital home; she may only leave for an urgent need or if staying causes hardship.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner
6 min
Obligation of Staying in the Marital Home During 'Iddah
Establishes the obligation of 'iddah in the marital home with Quranic and hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic and hadith proofs for the obligation of staying in the marital home during 'iddah and apply the rule to a scenario where the woman was away at the time of divorce.

Core Idea
A divorced or widowed woman must stay in the home she lived in during marriage for her entire 'iddah – that is wajib.

The waiting period ('iddah) after divorce or death has specific rules of residence. This passage from the Hidayah commentary establishes that the woman must remain in the marital home, not anywhere else. The proof is clear: the Quran commands 'do not expel them from their houses,' and the Prophet (ﷺ) explicitly instructed a widow to stay. We will unpack the meaning of 'house' and why this ruling is wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its hukm level
Read the opening statement: 'observing 'iddah is obligatory.' Recognize that the Hanafi school classifies this as wajib (obligatory but based on zanni evidence), not fard.
Wajib means sin if omitted, but evidence is ahad hadith.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Find the verse cited: 'wa la tukhrijuhunna min buyutihinna' (do not expel them from their houses). Note that it is a prohibition directed at the husband, but by implication, the wife must stay.
The imperative form indicates a clear command.
3
Define 'bayt' (house)
Examine the author's definition: the house is where she actually lived, regardless of ownership (owned, borrowed, or rented). This is key to applying the rule.
Ownership is irrelevant; residency is what matters.
4
Apply the rule to a practical scenario
Consider the example given: if the woman was at her parents' home when divorced, she must return to the marital home for 'iddah. This shows the obligation is tied to the marital residence.
Leaving the marital home without necessity is prohibited.
5
Confirm with the hadith proof
Read the hadith: the Prophet (ﷺ) told a woman whose husband was martyred to stay in her house until her 'iddah is complete. This reinforces the ruling for both divorce and death.
The hadith is a direct command, strengthening the wajib status.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
۱۹۳
باب العدة
عدت گذار نا واجب ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے و لا تخرجوهن من بیوتھن اور عورت کا بیت وہ کہلائے گا جس میں وہ رہتی تھی۔ اور سکنی یعنی رہنا عام ہے بطریق ملک رہتی ہو یا بطریق استعارہ یا بطریق استاجر ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر عورت اپنے میکے گئی ہوئی تھی ۔ پس شوہر نے وہیں رہتے ہوئے اس کو طلاق دے دی تو اس عورت پر واجب ہے کہ یہ لوٹ کر اپنے اسی گھر میں عدت گزارے جس میں یہ رہتی تھی۔ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس عورت سے جس کا شو ہر شہید ہوا تھایوں فرمایا کہ تو اپنے اس گھر میں ٹھہری رہ ۔ یہاں تک کہ اللہ تعالی کے فرمان کے مطابق تیری عدت پوری ہو جائے۔
Chapter of 'Iddah. Observing 'iddah is obligatory. The proof is that Allah Almighty said: "And do not expel them from their houses." And a woman's house is called that in which she lived. And dwelling (sukna) is general, whether she lived by ownership, or by borrowing, or by renting. This is why if a woman had gone to her parents' home, then her husband divorced her while she was there, it is obligatory upon her to return to that same house in which she lived and observe her 'iddah there. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the woman whose husband was martyred: "Stay in your house until the decree of Allah Almighty is fulfilled in your 'iddah."
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the obligation of 'iddah in the marital home. The author begins by stating that observing 'iddah is wajib (obligatory). The primary proof is the Quranic verse (65:1): 'wa la tukhrijuhunna min buyutihinna' (do not expel them from their houses). The term 'buyut' (houses) is defined as the dwelling where the woman actually resided during marriage, regardless of whether she owned it, borrowed it, or rented it. This definition is crucial: the obligation is tied to the physical place of residence, not ownership. The author then applies this: if the woman was at her parents' home when the divorce occurred, she must return to the marital home to complete her 'iddah. The second proof is a hadith from the Prophet (ﷺ) to a woman whose husband was martyred, commanding her to remain in her house until her 'iddah is complete. This reinforces that the obligation applies to both divorced and widowed women. Note that the Hanafi school holds this as wajib based on these texts; leaving the home without necessity would be a sin. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as this is the established position.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband, during which she cannot remarry.
سکنی (sukna): Dwelling or residing in a place, regardless of legal ownership.
بیت (bayt): The house where the woman lived with her husband during marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the term 'bayt' mean in the context of 'iddah residence according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Any house owned by the husband
B) The house where the woman lived with her husband
C) The woman's parental home
D) The nearest mosque

Key Takeaway
A woman must observe her 'iddah in the home she shared with her husband; it is wajib according to the Quran and Sunnah.

Moving from the Marital Home Due to Necessity
Explains exception when the woman's share in the house is insufficient and heirs evict her

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a widow may move from the marital home during 'iddah and apply the principle that excuses affect acts of worship.

Core Idea
A widow may move from the marital home if necessity prevents her from staying, such as insufficient space or eviction by heirs.

This lesson addresses an exception to the general obligation of a widow to remain in the marital home during the 'iddah period. The source explains that when her share of the house is too small and other heirs evict her, she is permitted to move due to a valid excuse (udhr). The ruling is supported by analogy to other cases of necessity and by the historical precedent of Umm Kulthum after the death of 'Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and the exception
The general ruling is that a widow must stay in the marital home during 'iddah. The exception is when necessity requires moving.
2
Determine the condition for the exception
The specific condition: her share of the house is insufficient for her to live in, and she is evicted by the other heirs from their shares.
3
Analyze the proof: the principle of udhr in acts of worship
Understand that the ruling is based on the principle that valid excuses alleviate obligations in acts of worship.
4
Examine the analogous cases
The source lists similar situations: fear for property, fear of collapse, inability to pay rent. These illustrate the breadth of 'udhr.
5
Review the historical precedent from the Sahaba
The case of Umm Kulthum (wife of 'Umar) being moved by 'Ali after 'Umar's death demonstrates the practical application of this exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و ان كان نصيبها من دار الميت لا يكفيها فاخرجها لورثة من نصيبهم انتقلت لأن هذا انتقال بعذر و العبادات توثر فيها الاعذار وصار كما اذا خافت على متاعها او خافت سقوط المنزل او كانت فيها باجر ولا تجد ما تؤديه ترجمہ اور اگر شوہر متوفی کے گھر میں سے اس عورت کا حصہ اس کے واسطے نا کافی ہو اور ورثہ اس کو اپنے حصہ سے نکال دیں تو یہ عورت منتقل ہو جائے ۔ کیونکہ ( یہ ) منتقل ہونا عذر کی وجہ سے ہے اور عبادات میں اعذار مؤثر ہوتے ہیں اور ( یہ ) ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ عورت کو اپنے سامان کا خوف ہوایا گھر کے گرنے کا خوف ہوا۔ یا اس گھر میں کرایہ پر رہتی تھی اور اب وہ کرایہ ادا نہیں کر سکتی ۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر متوفی کے مکان میں سے عورت کا حصہ اتنا نا کافی ہے کہ وہ اس میں نہیں رہ سکتی اور دوسرے ورثہ نے بھی اپنے حصتہ میں رہنے کی اجازت نہیں دی۔ تو ایسی صورت میں یہ عورت دوسرے کسی مکان میں منتقل ہو سکتی ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اسن کا منتقل ہونا عذر کی وجہ سے ہے اور عبادات میں عذر معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے یہاں بھی عذر معتبر ہوگا اور اس پر ایک دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت عمر کی شہادت کے بعد حضرت علی نے اپنی صاحبزادی ام کلثوم کو بیت العدت سے منتقل فرمایا۔ کیونکہ حضرت عمر خلیفہ ہونے کی وجہ سے سرکاری مکان میں سکونت پذیر تھے اور آپ کی شہادت کے بعد یہ مکان تیسرے خلیفہ حضرت عثمان غنی کے استعمال میں آ گیا۔ اس وجہ سے ام کلثوم ( زوجہ عمر ) کو اس مکان سے منتقل کرنے کی ضرورت پیش آئی۔ عینی شرح ہدایہ ) ( اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ عورت کو اس بات کا خوف ہو کہ میرا سامان چور اٹھالے جائیں گے۔ یا مکان گرنے کا ڈر ہو۔ یا یہ کہ اس مکان میں کرایہ پر تھی اور اب کرایہ ادا کرنے کی گنجائش نہیں رہی۔ تو جس طرح ان صورتوں میں معتدہ وفات کو منتقل ہونے کی اجازت ہے۔ اسی طرح مذکورہ بالا صورت میں بھی منتقل ہونے کی اجازت ہے۔
And if her share from the house of the deceased is insufficient for her, and the heirs remove her from their shares, she moves, because this is a transfer due to an excuse, and excuses affect acts of worship. It becomes like when she fears for her belongings, or fears the collapse of the house, or if she was in it by rent and cannot pay. Translation and explanation follow.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding an exception to the general obligation of staying in the marital home during 'iddah. The original matn (in Arabic) states that if the widowed woman's share in the deceased husband's house is too small to accommodate her, and the other heirs do not allow her to stay, she may move to another house. The reason is that this transfer is due to a valid excuse (udhr), and in acts of worship ('ibadat), excuses are taken into consideration. The commentary then provides an analogy: if a woman fears for her property, or fears the house might collapse, or if she was renting and can no longer pay rent, she may also move. The author further supports this with a historical precedent: after the martyrdom of 'Umar, 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) moved his daughter Umm Kulthum (widow of 'Umar) from the official residence because it was needed for the next caliph, 'Uthman. This shows that necessity allows relocation. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as it's a well-established exception. Note: this applies specifically to widows; for divorced women, similar principles may apply under genuine necessity.

Key Terms
عذر (udhr): A valid excuse that permits deviation from the general rule in acts of worship.
معتدہ وفات (mu'taddah wafat): A woman observing 'iddah due to the death of her husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which historical event is cited as proof that a widow may move from the marital home due to necessity?
A) The migration of the Prophet to Medina
B) 'Ali moving Umm Kulthum after 'Umar's death
C) The conquest of Mecca
D) The treaty of Hudaybiyyah

Key Takeaway
A widow may move from the marital home during 'iddah if her share is insufficient and she is evicted, because legitimate excuses (udhr) alleviate obligations in acts of worship.

Separation After Ba'in Divorce: The Curtain (Sutrah) Requirement
Rules on privacy and hijab between spouses during 'iddah after irrevocable divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the necessity of a curtain after ba'in divorce and apply the exception when the husband is fasiq.

Core Idea
After irrevocable divorce, a curtain is wajib; they may share a house unless the husband is fasiq.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the rules of privacy and living arrangements during the 'iddah period after a ba'in or triple divorce. The Hanafi school balances the obligation of 'iddah residence with the prohibition of unlawful intimacy, requiring a physical barrier. The key is whether the husband can be trusted to respect the prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is the former spouses living together during 'iddah after an irrevocable divorce. The ruling: a curtain (sutrah) is necessary (wajib).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is rational (dalil aqli): the husband acknowledges that she is haram (forbidden) for him, so he will avoid unlawful intimacy. Therefore, a curtain suffices to prevent seclusion (khalwa).
The dalil is not a scriptural text but a logical inference from the husband's acknowledgment.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The acknowledgment (i'tiraf) implies that the husband recognizes the prohibition and will refrain. Thus, the curtain prevents any accidental contact while allowing her to stay in the marital home for 'iddah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
If the husband is a fasiq (openly sinful) and there is fear of misconduct, the woman must leave the house. This is an exception due to the valid excuse (udhr).
The exception is based on necessity (darurah).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The preferred (awla) course is for the husband to leave, because the woman's stay during 'iddah is wajib while his stay is mubah (permissible). The wajib takes priority.
This tarjih is from Sahib al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ان وقعت لفرقة بطلاق بائن اوثلث لابد من سترة بينهما ثم لاباس لانه معترف بالحرمة الا ان يكون فاسقا يخاف عليها منه فحينئذ تخرج لانه عذر ولا تخرج عما انتقلت اليه والاولى ان يخرج هو ويتركها ترجمہ پھر اگر طلاق بائن یا تین طلاقوں کی وجہ سے فرقت واقع ہوئی تو دونوں کے درمیان پردہ ہونا ضروری ہے۔ پھر ایک گھر میں رہنے کا ) مضائقہ نہیں۔ کیونکہ شوہر اس کے حرام ہونے کا مقر ہے۔ لیکن اگر یہ مود فاسق ہو جس سے عورت پر خوف کیا جاتا ہے تو اس وقت یہ عورت اس مکان سے) نکل جائے ۔ کیونکہ یہ عذر ہے اور جس مکان میں منتقل ہو گئی وہاں سے نہ نکلے اور بہتر یہ ہے کہ مرد خود نکل جائے نکل جائے اور عورت کو ( یہیں ) چھوڑ دے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ زوجین کے درمیان اگر فرقت طلاق بائن یا تین طلاقوں کی وجہ سے واقع ہوئی تو عدت کے زمانے میں میاں بیوی کے درمیان پردہ ہونا ضروری ہے۔ پردہ ڈالنے کے بعد دونوں ایک مکان میں رہ سکتے ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرد اس عورت کے حرام ہونے کا مقر ہے۔ اسلئے وہ فعل حرام سے بچے گا۔ ہاں اگر شوہر فاسق ہو اور اس سے بدفعلی کا اندیشہ ہے تو اس صورت میں عورت کو میں اس مکان سے نکل جانا چاہئے۔ کیونکہ یہ شرعی عذر ہے اور جس مکان میں منتقل ہو کر چلی گئی اس سے بغیر عذرنہ نکلے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ زیادہ مناسب یہ ہے کہ اگر مکان ایک ہی ہو اور وہ بھی تنگ ہو تو اس صورت میں اس مکان سے عدت گذرنے تک کیلئے مرد کو نکل جانا چاہئے اور عورت اس مکان میں عدت گزارے۔ کیونکہ شوہر کے مکان میں اس معندہ عورت کا ٹھہرنا واجب ہے اور مرد کا ٹھہر نا مباح ہے اور واجب کی رعایت ادنی ہے۔
Then if separation occurs by ba'in divorce or three divorces, a curtain is necessary between them. Then there is no harm [in staying in the same house], because he acknowledges the prohibition. Except if he is a fasiq (sinner) from whom she fears [misconduct], then she should leave, because it is an excuse. And she should not leave the house she moved to. And it is better that he leaves and leaves her [in the house]. Translation and explanation follow.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation when separation occurs due to a ba'in divorce (one that does not allow revocability without a new marriage) or three divorces (which make the woman irrevocably forbidden until she marries another and is divorced). During the 'iddah period, it is necessary (la budda) to have a sutrah (curtain or barrier) between the spouses. However, they may still live in the same house after placing the curtain, because the husband acknowledges that marital relations are now haram (forbidden) and will avoid them. But if the husband is a fasiq (openly sinful) and there is fear of misconduct (zina), the woman should leave that house, as this is a valid excuse. Once she moves to another house, she should not leave that new place without another valid excuse. The author, Sahib al-Hidayah (i.e., al-Marghinani), states that the preferred (awla) course is for the husband to leave the house, not the woman, because the woman's staying in the marital home during 'iddah is wajib (obligatory), while the husband's staying is merely mubah (permissible). Since the wajib should be prioritized, it is better for the man to move out, leaving the woman to complete her 'iddah in the house. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, with the mufta bihi position being that the curtain suffices if the man is reliable, but if he is fasiq, the woman may leave.

Key Terms
سترة (sutrah): A physical barrier or curtain placed between the former spouses to prevent direct interaction.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately and does not allow revocation without a new marriage.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who openly commits major sins or persists in minor sins, making him untrustworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred (awla) action according to Sahib al-Hidayah when the house is cramped after a ba'in divorce?
A) The woman should leave the house
B) The man should leave the house
C) Both should leave and rent separate houses
D) They should continue living together without a curtain

Key Takeaway
After irrevocable divorce, a curtain is obligatory; if the husband is trustworthy, they may stay together, but if he is fasiq, she must leave, and it is preferred that the man leaves.

Woman Returning to Her City When Divorced on a Short Trip
Ruling for a woman divorced while traveling with her husband away from home

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a woman divorced while traveling may return to her city to observe 'iddah, and explain why it is not considered a new journey.

Core Idea
A divorced woman may return home if less than three days away, as that is a continuation, not a new journey.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the situation of a woman who is divorced or widowed while traveling with her husband. It clarifies that if the distance to her hometown is less than three days' travel, she may return to complete her 'iddah there. The ruling is based on the principle that a short return is not considered a new journey, which would be prohibited during 'iddah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Note that the woman is traveling with her husband (e.g., to Makkah) and either receives a triple divorce or becomes widowed.
This is a specific situation where the woman is already on a permissible journey with her husband.
2
Check the distance condition
Determine if the place where the divorce/death occurred is less than three days' travel from her original city (misr).
Three days' travel is the minimum distance for a full journey (safar) in Hanafi fiqh.
3
State the ruling
If the distance is less than three days, she returns to her city to observe 'iddah. If it is three days or more, she must stay where she is.
This is a wajib obligation based on the need to observe 'iddah in her residence.
4
Understand the rationale
The return is considered a continuation of the original journey (بنا), not a new beginning (ابتداء). Therefore, it does not count as a prohibited journey during 'iddah.
This principle prevents the prohibition from being violated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان جعلا بينهما امرأة ثقة تقدر على الحيلولة فحسن وان ضاق عليهما المنزل فلتخرج والاولى خروجه واذا خرجت المرأة مع زوجها الى مكة فطلقها ثلثا اومات عنها فى غير مصروف ان كان بينها وبين مصرها اقل من ثلثة ايام رجعت الى مصرها لانه ليس بابتداء الخروج معنى بل هو بناء ترجمہ اور اگر دونوں نے اپنے درمیان ایک ثقہ عورت کو حائل کر دیا، جس کو درمیانی روک کی قدرت ہے تو اچھا ہے اور اگر وہ مکان دونوں پر تنگ ہو تو عورت کو نکل جانا چاہئے اور بہتر مرد کا نکلنا ہے اور اگر کوئی عورت اپنے شوہر کے ساتھ مکہ معظمہ تک چلی پس شوہر نے اس کو غیر مصر میں تین طلاقیں دیں۔ یا شو ہر اس کو چھوڑ کر مرا۔ پس اگر ( اس مقام سے ) عورت اور اس کے شہر کے درمیان تین دن سے کم مسافت ہو تو اپنے شہر کی طرف لوٹ آئے۔ کیونکہ یہ نکلنا معنی ابتدائی نکلنا نہیں بلکہ (سفر اول پر مبنی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر زوجین نے اپنے درمیان کسی قابل اعتماد عورت کو حائل کر لیا جس کو درمیانی روک کی قدرت ہے تو اچھا ہے اور اگر وہ مکان دونوں پر تنگ ہو کہ دونوں کا رہنا مشکل ہے تو عورت کیلئے نکل کر دوسرے مکان کی طرف منتقل ہونا جائز ہے۔ لیکن زیادہ بہتر یہ ہے، کہ مرد نکل جائے اور عورت اسی مکان میں عدت گزارے۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عورت اپنے شوہر کے ساتھ مکہ معظمہ کی طرف چلی۔ پھر شوہر نے راستہ میں ایسی جگہ جہاں آبادی ہو اس کو تین طلاقیں دے دیں یا شوہر مر گیا۔ پس اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر اس مقام ہے اس عورت کے شہر تک تین دن سے کم مسافت ہے تو یہ لوٹ کر اپنے شہر کی طرف آجائے۔ اس لئے کہ یہ نکلنا ابتدائی سفر نہیں ہے بلکہ اپنے پہلے سفر کی بنا پر ہے۔
And if they place between them a trustworthy woman who is able to act as a barrier, that is good. And if the house is cramped for both, then the woman should leave, but it is better for him to leave. And if a woman went out with her husband to Mecca, and he divorced her three times or died on her in a non-Egyptian place, and if between her and her city there is less than three days' distance, she should return to her city, because this going out is not a beginning of travel in meaning, but rather a continuation.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct but related issues. The first part repeats the ruling about a trustworthy woman as a barrier (hijab) and the preference for the man to leave the house if it is cramped. The second part presents a new ruling: if a woman traveled with her husband to Mecca (or any journey) and he divorced her (three times) or died while they were at a place that is less than a three-day journey from her original city (misr), then she should return to her city to complete her 'iddah. The reason given is that this is not considered a new journey; it is a continuation of the original travel. In Hanafi fiqh, a woman observing 'iddah should not undertake a journey of three days or more (safar) unnecessarily. However, since she was already on a permissible journey with her husband, returning to her city when the distance is short is allowed and even required to observe 'iddah properly at home. If the distance were three days or more, the ruling might differ (she would need to complete 'iddah where she is). This is a ruling statement without explicit proof, but it is based on the principle that 'iddah in the home is wajib and travel for less than three days is not considered a full safar that would prevent her from moving. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): The woman's original city or hometown.
ثلثة ايام (thalathatu ayyam): Three days' travel, which is the minimal distance for a full journey (safar) in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition may a woman return to her city after being divorced while traveling with her husband?
A) If the distance to her city is less than three days' travel
B) If she has no relatives with her
C) If she is divorced for the first time
D) If she is pregnant

Key Takeaway
A woman divorced or widowed while traveling with her husband may return to her city if the place is less than three days away, because her return is a continuation of the original journey.

Ruling on Staying in the Same House During 'Iddah After Ba'in or Triple Divorce
Ruling on staying in same house after ba'in or triple talaq with hijab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on living arrangements during 'iddah after a ba'in or triple divorce, and identify when the woman may leave the marital home.

Core Idea
After a ba'in divorce, the woman must stay in the marital home for 'iddah, but may leave if the husband is sinful.

Many assume that after a divorce, the woman must immediately leave her husband's house. This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the Hanafi position: she must stay for her 'iddah, but with observed hijab. Only if the husband is a fasiq and there is genuine fear of misconduct may she leave. The ruling is based on the rational principle that the husband, knowing the woman is forbidden to him, will avoid intimacy. This lesson unpacks the conditions and preferences in this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is the spouses living in the same house during the woman's 'iddah after a ba'in or triple divorce. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) for them to stay together, provided they maintain hijab (seclusion).
The woman's own stay in the marital home is actually wajib according to the text.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author provides a rational proof: the husband is assured (muqirr) that the woman is haram for him, so he will avoid any forbidden act. This rational certainty makes it safe for them to cohabit with hijab.
The proof is classified as dalil aqli (rational evidence), not a textual proof from Quran or Sunnah.
3
Note the exception
If the husband is fasiq (sinful) and there is fear that he may transgress, the woman may leave the house because this is a valid excuse (shar'i 'udhr).
The exception applies only when there is genuine fear; otherwise, she must stay.
4
Evaluate the preferred action
The author of Al-Hidayah states that if the house is narrow, it is better (afdal) for the man to leave and let the woman complete her 'iddah, because her stay is wajib and his is mubah, and the wajib should be considered first.
This prioritization reflects the Hanafi fiqh principle of giving precedence to obligations over permissible acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العدة ۱۹۴ اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم ترجمہ پھر اگر طلاق بائن یا تین طلاقوں کی وجہ سے فرقت واقع ہوئی تو دونوں کے درمیان پردہ ہونا ضروری ہے۔ پھر ایک گھر میں رہنے کا ) مضائقہ نہیں۔ کیونکہ شوہر اس کے حرام ہونے کا مقر ہے۔ لیکن اگر یہ مود فاسق ہو جس سے عورت پر خوف کیا جاتا ہے تو اس وقت یہ عورت اس مکان سے) نکل جائے ۔ کیونکہ یہ عذر ہے اور جس مکان میں منتقل ہو گئی وہاں سے نہ نکلے اور بہتر یہ ہے کہ مرد خود نکل جائے نکل جائے اور عورت کو ( یہیں ) چھوڑ دے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ زوجین کے درمیان اگر فرقت طلاق بائن یا تین طلاقوں کی وجہ سے واقع ہوئی تو عدت کے زمانے میں میاں بیوی کے درمیان پردہ ہونا ضروری ہے۔ پردہ ڈالنے کے بعد دونوں ایک مکان میں رہ سکتے ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرد اس عورت کے حرام ہونے کا مقر ہے۔ اسلئے وہ فعل حرام سے بچے گا۔ ہاں اگر شوہر فاسق ہو اور اس سے بدفعلی کا اندیشہ ہے تو اس صورت میں عورت کو میں اس مکان سے نکل جانا چاہئے۔ کیونکہ یہ شرعی عذر ہے اور جس مکان میں منتقل ہو کر چلی گئی اس سے بغیر عذرنہ نکلے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ زیادہ مناسب یہ ہے کہ اگر مکان ایک ہی ہو اور وہ بھی تنگ ہو تو اس صورت میں اس مکان سے عدت گذرنے تک کیلئے مرد کو نکل جانا چاہئے اور عورت اس مکان میں عدت گزارے۔ کیونکہ شوہر کے مکان میں اس معندہ عورت کا ٹھہرنا واجب ہے اور مرد کا ٹھہر نا مباح ہے اور واجب کی رعایت ادنی ہے۔
Chapter of 'Iddah 194 Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 5 Translation: Then if separation occurred due to ba'in divorce or triple divorce, hijab between them is necessary. Then there is no harm in living in one house because the husband is assured of her being haram. But if this husband is fasiq from whom danger is feared for the woman, then at that time this woman should leave this house because it is an excuse. And from the house she moved to, she should not leave. And it is better that the man himself leaves and leaves the woman here. Explanation: The scenario is that if separation between spouses occurred due to ba'in divorce or triple divorce, during the period of 'iddah, hijab between husband and wife is necessary. After putting the hijab, both can live in one house. The proof is that the husband is assured of her being haram. Therefore, he will avoid the forbidden act. Yes, if the husband is fasiq and there is fear of immorality, then in that case the woman should leave from there because it is a valid excuse. And from the house she moved to, she should not leave without an excuse. The author of Hidayah says: It is more appropriate that if there is only one house and it is also narrow, then in that case the man should leave until the 'iddah passes and the woman should spend her 'iddah in that house because the woman's staying in the husband's house is wajib and the man's staying is mubah, and consideration of wajib is better.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on living arrangements during the 'iddah period after a ba'in or triple divorce. It is a ruling with a rational proof. The text begins by stating that after such a divorce, the spouses must observe hijab (seclusion) from each other. However, they may continue to live in the same house because the husband knows the woman is now forbidden to him, so he will avoid intimacy. If the husband is a fasiq (sinner) and there is fear that he might transgress, the woman may leave the house as a valid excuse. The commentary further explains that if the house is narrow, it is better for the man to leave and let the woman complete her 'iddah there, because her staying in the husband's house is wajib (obligatory) while his staying is merely mubah (permissible). The proof is rational: the husband's awareness of the prohibition ensures safety, and the recommendation prioritizes the wajib over the mubah.

Key Terms
عدت (‘iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before she can remarry.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): A type of divorce that is irrevocable; the husband cannot take his wife back without a new marriage and her having been married to another man (in case of triple divorce).
پردہ (purdah): A screen or partition; here meaning the spouses must avoid being alone together and observe modesty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Whenever she wants.
C) Only if her husband gives permission.
D) She must leave immediately.

Key Takeaway
The woman's stay in the marital home during 'iddah after a ba'in divorce is wajib, but she may leave if the husband is fasiq, and it is better for the husband to leave if the house is narrow.

Appointing a Trustworthy Woman as Barrier During 'Iddah
Ruling statement on separation during 'iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on appointing a trustworthy woman as a barrier during 'iddah and identify the recommended course of action when the house is narrow.

Core Idea
Appointing a trustworthy woman is commendable, but in a narrow house, the woman's leaving is appropriate and the man's leaving is better.

During the 'iddah period of a ba'in divorce, the spouses are not permitted to be alone together. The Hanafi school offers practical guidance on maintaining proper separation while under the same roof. This passage discusses the commendable act of appointing a trustworthy woman as a chaperone, and what to do if the house is too small to prevent impropriety.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two scenarios: (1) appointing a trustworthy woman as a barrier, and (2) when the house is narrow.
2
Determine the ruling for each
For scenario 1, the ruling is 'hasan' (good/commendable). For scenario 2, the woman should leave, and it is better for the man to leave.
The term 'hasan' indicates a sunnah or mustahabb act, not an obligation.
3
Understand the underlying principles
The woman's obligation to stay in the marital home during 'iddah is default, but when the house is too narrow to maintain proper hijab, she is permitted to leave. The man's leaving is preferred because he is not bound by that obligation.
This reflects the Hanafi priority of avoiding fitna over strict adherence to residence.

Source Text

And if the house is narrow for them, then the woman should leave, and it is better for the man to leave. Translation: And if both place a trustworthy woman between them, who has the power to prevent, then it is good. And if the house is narrow for both, then the woman should leave, and the man's leaving is better.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the recommendation of appointing a trustworthy woman as a barrier between the divorced spouses during the 'iddah period. It is a ruling statement without an explicit proof. The text states that if they appoint a trustworthy woman who can physically separate them, it is commendable (hasan). If the house is too narrow for both to stay with proper hijab, the woman should leave because her staying is wajib, but it is better for the man to leave since the woman's obligation to stay in the husband's house takes precedence. This ruling follows from the previous discussion on the permissibility of staying together.

Key Terms
ثقہ عورت (siqah 'aurat): A trustworthy woman who can be relied upon to prevent any impropriety between the spouses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Woman Divorced En Route: Return or Continue Based on Distance
Ruling on woman divorced en route: return if less than three days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distance rule to determine whether a woman divorced during travel must return to her city or has a choice.

Core Idea
A woman divorced en route must return home if less than three days away; if exactly three days, she may choose, but returning is better.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling for a woman who is divorced or widowed while traveling with her husband. The key factor is the distance from the place of divorce to her home city. The ruling balances the obligation to observe 'iddah in the marital home with the dangers of travel. The proof is rational: the return journey is a continuation of the original travel, not a new journey.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two scenarios based on the distance from the place of divorce to the woman's city: less than three days' journey, and three days' journey.
The third scenario (destination closer than city) is also mentioned but is a straightforward application.
2
Apply the distance rule
If the distance to her city is less than three days, returning is wajib (obligatory). If it is exactly three days, she has a choice (mubah) to return or continue, but returning is better.
The measure of three days is based on the Hanafi definition of travel (safar).
3
Understand the rational proof
The proof (dalil aqli) is that the woman's journey home is not a new departure but a continuation of the original travel. Thus, it does not constitute a separate travel that would require a mahram.
The text states: 'laisa bi-ibtida' al-khuruj ma'nan bal huwa bina'' (it is not a new initiation but a construction).
4
Note the preference for returning
Even when she has a choice, returning to her city to complete 'iddah in the marital home is better (awla). This respects the general rule that 'iddah should be observed in the husband's house.
The text says: 'illa anna al-ruju' awla li-yakun al-i'tidad fi manzil al-zawj'.
5
Consider the exception when destination is closer
If her city is three days away but her destination (e.g., Makkah) is less than three days away, she should go to the destination because it is safer.
This is a sub-case mentioned in the explanation.

The ruling is that if the distance from that place to her city is less than three days, she returns to her city and completes her 'iddah there, whether the distance to her destination is three days or less. The proof is that this departure is not an initial departure but based on the first journey. And if it is a three days' journey, she may return or continue, whether she has a mahram or not. Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on a woman who, while traveling with her husband to Makkah, is divorced by triple talaq or widowed en route. It is a ruling supported by rational proof. The text presents two scenarios. First, if the distance from the place of divorce to her city is less than three days' travel, she must return to her city to complete her 'iddah. The proof is that her journey is not a new departure but a continuation of the original journey, so returning home is not a new travel. Second, if the distance is exactly three days (or more?), she has a choice: she may either return to her city or continue to her destination. This applies even without a mahram. The proof is that staying alone in a wilderness is more dangerous than traveling. However, returning is preferable so that she completes her 'iddah in the husband's house. If her city is three days away but her destination is less than three days, she should go to the destination. The ruling balances the obligation of staying in the marital home for 'iddah with the safety concerns during travel.

Key Terms
مسافت (masafat): Distance measured by travel time (three days).
مصر (misr): A city or town that is the woman's home.

Leaving the City During 'Iddah with a Mahram: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on leaving city during 'iddah with mahram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on leaving the city during 'iddah with a mahram and explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) behind each view.

Core Idea
The presence of a mahram does not automatically lift the restriction of 'iddah; the stronger prohibition governs.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a woman in 'iddah of a ba'in divorce or widowhood must remain in the marital home and cannot travel even for less than three days without a mahram. But what if she has a mahram available? Can she leave the city before her 'iddah ends? The Hanafi school has a nuanced internal disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). This lesson unpacks their arguments and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act in question
The act is a woman in 'iddah (ba'in or widow) leaving the city (misr) where she resides before completing her 'iddah, while accompanied by a mahram.
The dispute is only about leaving with a mahram; without a mahram, all agree it is prohibited.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and his proof
Abu Hanifa says she must not leave until 'iddah is complete, even with a mahram. His proof: the prohibition of 'iddah is stronger than the prohibition of traveling without a mahram. Since a woman in 'iddah cannot even travel short distances (less than three days) without a mahram (which a non-mu'taddah can), the presence of a mahram does not remove the 'iddah restriction.
This is a rational argument comparing the strength of two prohibitions.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say she may leave with a mahram before completing 'iddah. Their proof: the act of leaving is itself permissible to avoid loneliness and solitude, which is a valid excuse. The prohibition of travel is lifted by the mahram, so the only remaining restriction is the duty to stay in the home, but that duty can be overridden by necessity.
They consider the need to travel as a legitimate reason.
4
Compare the two arguments
The key difference is whether the 'iddah prohibition is seen as absolute (Abu Hanifa) or whether the presence of a mahram can remove the travel restriction, leaving only the duty to observe 'iddah wherever she goes (Sahibayn).
Both are valid ijtihad within the Hanafi school.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
In practice, under Abu Hanifa's view, she must remain in the city; under the Sahibayn, she may travel with a mahram if needed. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the school is Abu Hanifa's view, based on the principle of caution in 'iddah matters.
However, in cases of genuine hardship, some later fatwa works apply the Sahibayn's view as a concession.

قال الا ان يكون طلقها اومات عنها زوجها فى مصر فانها لاتخرج حتى تعتدثم تخرج ان كان لها محرم وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقال ابويوسف و محمد ان كان معها محرم فلابأس بان تخرج من المصر قبل ان تعتدلهما أن نفس الخروج مباح دفعالا ذى الغربة ووحشة الوحدة وهذا عذر وانما الحرمة للسفر وقد ارتفعت بالمحرم وله ان العدة امنع من الخروج من عدم المحرم فان للمراة ان تخرج الى مادون السفر بغير محرم و ليس للمعتدة ذالک فلما حرم عليها الخروج الى السفر بغير المحرم ففى العدة الأولى ترجمہ امام محمد نے (جامع صغیر میں ) فرمایا۔ لیکن اگر شوہر نے اس عورت کو کسی شہر میں تین طلاقیں دیں یا چھوڑ مرا ہو ۔ تو عورت . ( اس شہر سے باہر نہ نکلے ۔ یہاں تک کہ اپنی عدت پوری کرلے۔ پھر نکلے بشرطیکہ کوئی محرم ساتھ ہوا اور یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے کہا اگر عورت کے ساتھ کوئی محرم موجود ہو تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں کہ وہ عدت پوری کرنے سے پہلے اس شہر سے چلی جاوے۔
He said: But if her husband divorced her or died from her in a city, then she should not leave until she completes her 'iddah, then she may leave if she has a mahram. And this is according to Abu Hanifah. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: If she has a mahram with her, then there is no harm that she leaves the city before completing her 'iddah. Their argument is that the very act of leaving is permissible to repel the fear of being alone and the loneliness of solitude, and this is a valid excuse. And the prohibition is for travel, and it is removed by the presence of a mahram. And his (Abu Hanifa's) argument is that the 'iddah is more prohibitive than the lack of a mahram. Indeed, a woman may travel less than three days without a mahram, but a woman in 'iddah does not have that. So when travel without a mahram is prohibited for her, then during the 'iddah it is even more so.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a woman in 'iddah of a ba'in divorce or widowhood may leave the city before completing her 'iddah if she has a mahram. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that she must complete her 'iddah in the city and cannot leave even with a mahram. His proof is that the prohibition of 'iddah (staying in the marital home) is stronger than the prohibition of traveling without a mahram. Since a woman may normally travel less than three days without a mahram, but a woman in 'iddah is prohibited from even that, the presence of a mahram does not lift the restriction of 'iddah. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that the need to travel is a valid excuse to avoid solitude and loneliness, and the prohibition of travel is lifted by the presence of a mahram. Therefore, she may leave the city with a mahram before completing her 'iddah. The text does not specify the mufta bihi position, but typically the view of Abu Hanifa is preferred in strict practice.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A male relative whom the woman is permanently forbidden to marry (e.g., father, brother, son).
مصر (misr): A city where the woman resides.

C) Yes, but only if she has no mahram.
D) No, under any circumstances.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on whether a mahram allows a woman to leave the city before completing 'iddah; Abu Hanifa's stricter view is generally relied upon.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on a Woman in 'Iddah Leaving the City
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'iddah and mahram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding a woman in 'iddah leaving the city, explain their respective proofs, and evaluate the practical difference.

Core Idea
The 'iddah restriction overrides the mahram's permission for travel according to Abu Hanifa.

In this passage, we encounter a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn gives the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: a woman in 'iddah from three divorces or widowhood must remain in the city until her 'iddah ends, even if a mahram is available. However, the two students of Abu Hanifa — Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) — dissent. Their disagreement revolves around whether the presence of a mahram lifts the prohibition of travel during 'iddah or whether the 'iddah itself creates a stronger prohibition that cannot be overridden. By tracing each side's proof, you will learn how the Hanafi school reasons through conflicting analogies.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify the ruling attributed to Abu Hanifa: the woman must not leave the city until 'iddah is complete. After 'iddah, she may leave only with a mahram.
This is the position presented in the matn.
2
Identify the opposing view (Sahibayn)
State the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: she may leave the city before completing 'iddah if a mahram is present.
The Sahibayn are the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
Understand their dalil: exiting the city is permissible (mubah) to avoid hardship and loneliness. The prohibition is only on travel (safar), and the mahram removes that prohibition.
They analogize to a woman without 'iddah who may travel less than three days without a mahram.
4
Analyse Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa's proof: the prohibition on leaving during 'iddah is stronger than the prohibition on traveling without a mahram. Since a woman normally may go short distances without a mahram but a woman in 'iddah cannot, the prohibition during 'iddah is a fortiori (awlā) greater.
This is an argument from the greater to the lesser (qiyās al-awlā).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the woman stays until 'iddah ends. Under the Sahibayn, she may travel earlier if a mahram is available.
The tarjih (preferred view) is not explicitly given, but Abu Hanifa's view is the one in the matn and is likely mufta bihi.

امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بغیر محرم سفر کرنے کے مقابلہ میں عدت میں نکلنا زیادہ ممنوع ہے۔ چنانچہ عورت مدت سفر سے کم بغیر محرم کے سفر کر سکتی ہے۔ لیکن معدہ کیلئے یہ بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ پس جب عورت کیلئے بغیر محرم کے مدت سفر کی مقدار سفر کرنا حرام ہے۔ تو عدت میں اس عورت کا سفر کرنا بدرجہ اولی حرام ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم ۔ جمیل احمد غفرلہ
The husband gave three divorces or died leaving her in a city: then the woman will not leave until she completes her 'iddah, then she may leave if she has a mahram. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: If she has a mahram, there is no problem in her leaving the city before completing her 'iddah. Their proof: The act of exiting itself is permissible to dispel the hardship of travel and the loneliness of solitude, and this is an excuse. The prohibition was only for travel, and that has been removed by the mahram. His (Abu Hanifa's) proof: The prohibition of leaving during 'iddah is greater than the prohibition of traveling without a mahram, because a woman may travel less than the travel distance without a mahram, but a woman in 'iddah may not even do that. So when traveling without a mahram is prohibited, leaving during 'iddah is even more prohibited.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a woman who is given three divorces or becomes a widow while in a city. The ruling from the matn (Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad) is that she must not leave the city until she completes her 'iddah, and only then may she leave if she has a mahram. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad himself) hold that if a mahram is present, she may leave the city even before completing her 'iddah. Their reasoning is that the mere act of exiting the city is permissible to avoid the hardship and loneliness of staying in an unfamiliar place; the prohibition is only on the travel itself, and that prohibition is removed by the presence of a mahram. In other words, the mahram makes the travel permissible, just as a woman may travel less than the distance of travel (safar) without a mahram. Abu Hanifa's counterargument is that the prohibition of leaving during 'iddah is stronger than the prohibition of traveling without a mahram. This is because a woman may normally travel a short distance (less than three days) without a mahram, but a woman in 'iddah is prohibited from such movement even within the city. Therefore, if traveling the full three-day distance without a mahram is prohibited, then for a woman in 'iddah, any travel (even with a mahram) is even more prohibited, since the 'iddah itself creates a stronger restriction. The passage thus highlights a clear divergence of opinion within the Hanafi school on the interaction between the obligations of 'iddah and the permissibility of travel with a mahram.

Key Terms
عدت ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before she may remarry.
محرم (mahram): A male relative whom a woman is permanently forbidden to marry, such as a father, brother, son, etc.
مصر (misr): A city or settled area, as opposed to a desert or wilderness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) She may leave immediately if she has a mahram.
B) She must remain in the city until her 'iddah is complete.
C) She may leave only if she has no mahram.
D) She may leave only to return to her hometown.

Key Takeaway
The 'iddah restriction on movement is stronger than the mahram's permission for travel, according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
