Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Leaving 'Iddah Residence with a Mahram
Intra-Hanafi dispute on leaving 'iddah residence with mahram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on a woman in 'iddah leaving her residence with a mahram, explain the evidence for each, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
A woman in 'iddah cannot leave even with a mahram; Sahibayn allow it due to hardship.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement: can a woman in 'iddah travel from the settlement where her separation occurred if she has a mahram with her? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that 'iddah confinement is so strict that even with a mahram, leaving is not permitted. The two companions (Sahibayn) argue that the hardship of travel and loneliness justifies an exception when a mahram is present. Understanding this dispute clarifies the hierarchy of prohibitions and the method of tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
State the majority Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa's view) clearly. She must remain in the house of 'iddah until its completion, and even a mahram does not permit earlier departure.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing view
Identify the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) as the opponents within the Hanafi school and state their view: she may leave before 'iddah ends if accompanied by a mahram.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Analyse the opponents' proof
Break down the Sahibayn's evidence: exiting is permissible to remove hardship, and the prohibition of travel is negated by the mahram. They compare it to traveling a short distance without a mahram, which is allowed.
The key is 'hardship' as a valid excuse.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Explain Abu Hanifa's response: the 'iddah adds an extra prohibition, so leaving is more strictly forbidden than ordinary travel without a mahram. Since a non-'iddah woman cannot travel a long distance without a mahram, a woman in 'iddah cannot even travel a short distance, even with a mahram.
The concept of 'priority of prohibition' (awlawiyyah) is used.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: under Sahibayn's view, she can travel with a mahram; under Abu Hanifa's view, she must stay. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, so in practice she must remain.
This affects the fatwa given to women in such situations.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم

امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بغیر محرم سفر کرنے کے مقابلہ میں عدت میں نکلنا زیادہ ممنوع ہے۔ چنانچہ عورت مدت سفر سے کم بغیر محرم کے سفر کر سکتی ہے۔ لیکن معدہ کیلئے یہ بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ پس جب عورت کیلئے بغیر محرم کے مدت سفر کی مقدار سفر کرنا حرام ہے۔ تو عدت میں اس عورت کا سفر کرنا بدرجہ اولی حرام ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم ۔ جمیل احمد غفرلہ
Chapter of 'Iddah. 194. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Five. The evidence of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that merely exiting (from the house of 'iddah) to travel is permissible to remove the hardship of travel and the loneliness of seclusion, and this is an excuse. However, travel was forbidden (without a mahram), but that (prohibition) is removed due to the presence of a mahram. Purpose: And the evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa is that leaving during 'iddah without a mahram by traveling is even more forbidden (by priority). Explanation: Previously, the author said that if the separation occurred in a non-city (wilderness) and the woman's homeland and her destination from where she was going are both a distance of three days each, then she has the choice: either return to her homeland or proceed to the intended destination. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) made an exception to this ruling and said that if the separation occurred in a settlement during travel, then this woman should not leave that city (settlement) until she completes her 'iddah. Then after completing her 'iddah, if she has a mahram with her, she can leave. This is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions said that if this woman has a mahram with her, then there is no harm in leaving the city even before completing her 'iddah. The evidence of the two companions is that merely exiting to remove the hardship of travel and loneliness is permissible and lawful. Thus, according to consensus, leaving for less than the travel distance is legally permitted. The conclusion is that the hardship of travel and loneliness is an excuse, and due to the excuse, it is permissible for the woman in 'iddah to leave the house of 'iddah. At most, you can say that traveling the full distance is forbidden, then we will respond that the occurrence of travel is removed due to the presence of a mahram. Thus, traveling with a mahram becomes like traveling without a mahram for less than the travel distance. The evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa is that leaving during 'iddah is more prohibited compared to traveling without a mahram. Thus, a woman can travel without a mahram for less than the travel distance, but for a woman in 'iddah, even that is not permissible. So when traveling the full distance without a mahram is forbidden for a woman, then for a woman in 'iddah to travel is even more forbidden (by priority). And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad, may He forgive him.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute explaining the different rulings of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding a woman in 'iddah leaving her residence without a mahram. The context is a woman who is separated from her husband while traveling. Imam Muhammad earlier ruled that if the separation occurs in a settlement during travel, the woman must stay in that settlement until her 'iddah ends, and only then may leave with a mahram. Imam Abu Hanifa agrees with this. However, Sahibayn differ: they allow the woman to leave the settlement even before completing 'iddah if she has a mahram with her. Their proof: the act of exiting itself is permissible to relieve travel hardship and loneliness; these are valid excuses. They argue that leaving for a distance less than full travel (three days) is agreed upon as permissible, so with a mahram the prohibition of travel is removed. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: since traveling without a mahram for three days is forbidden, leaving during 'iddah (even with a mahram) is even more forbidden because 'iddah confinement takes precedence. The ritual of 'iddah is an additional prohibition beyond the general prohibition of traveling without mahram. The text presents Sahibayn's objection that exiting is permissible, and Abu Hanifa's response that 'iddah elevates the prohibition. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but in the Hanafi school, the ruling of Abu Hanifa is generally preferred in this matter. The passage illustrates the principle of 'al-walad li al-firash' indirectly, but the main focus is on the ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before she can remarry.
محرم (mahram): A male relative whom a woman is permanently forbidden to marry (e.g., father, brother, son).
خروج (khuruj): The act of leaving or exiting from the house of 'iddah.
مفارقت (mufaraqat): Separation, specifically here referring to the separation of the couple (by death or divorce) during travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is it more forbidden for a woman in 'iddah to travel even with a mahram compared to a woman not in 'iddah traveling without a mahram?
A) Because 'iddah is an additional restriction that makes leaving more prohibited.
B) Because traveling with a mahram is still forbidden for all women.
C) Because she must stay in the house until she remarries.
D) Because leaving during 'iddah invalidates the 'iddah.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa that a woman in 'iddah must not leave her residence even with a mahram is the mufta bihi, due to the greater restriction of 'iddah over general travel prohibitions.

Establishing Lineage After Revocable Divorce: Timing and Certainty
Explains ruling with rational proof on lineage and revocation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for establishing lineage (nasab) after revocable divorce by distinguishing the two scenarios based on the timing of birth and the husband's right to revoke.

Core Idea
Lineage is established on possibility; revocation requires certainty of conception after divorce.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains how a child's paternity is determined when a revocably divorced woman gives birth. The Hanafi school balances the child's right to lineage with the husband's right to revoke (ruj'ah), using the maximum pregnancy period of two years as a key criterion. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the role of doubt and certainty in family law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is establishing lineage (nasab) of a child born to a woman in revocable divorce (talaq raj'i). The ruling is that lineage is established (sahih) in all scenarios, but revocation (ruj'ah) is dependent on the timing of birth.
Lineage is always established if the child is born within the maximum pregnancy period (2 years Hanafi) from the divorce.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is rational (dalil aqli): based on the maximum pregnancy period of two years, the permissibility of intercourse during the iddah of revocable divorce, and the negation of fornication (zina).
No explicit Quran or Hadith is cited; the reasoning is from established legal principles.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key link: If the child is born within two years, conception could have occurred before or after divorce, so revocation is doubtful (does not occur). If born after two years, conception must be after divorce, so revocation is certain (occurs).
Certainty of conception after divorce is derived from the maximum pregnancy period rule.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The two-year maximum pregnancy period is specific to Hanafis. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i, Maliki) generally hold 1 year or less, which may affect lineage rulings in similar cases.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on differing views on gestation limits.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Al-Marghinani (in Al-Hidayah) adopts the two-year rule based on reliable transmissions and the principle of precaution (ihtiyat) for lineage.
The mufta bihi is as stated in the text: both scenarios establish lineage; revocation depends on birth timing.

Chapter on Establishing Lineage. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Sharh Hidayah Volume Five. And the child's lineage (from the husband) is established. Because the seed was found in marriage or in the waiting period, and the husband will not be one who returns (by revocable divorce). Because the seed could be before divorce or after divorce. Therefore, due to doubt, the husband will not be considered as returning. And if that woman gives birth after more than two years, then revocation will occur. Because the seed is after divorce and it is apparent that the sperm is from that man. Because fornication from the woman is negated. So he will become one who returns through intercourse. Explanation: The scenario is that a woman whom her husband gave a revocable divorce. She gives birth at two years or more than two years from the time of divorce, then the child's lineage from the husband will be established, provided that the woman did not acknowledge the passing of the waiting period. The reason is that it is possible that this woman has an extended period of purity and due to the prolongation of purity her waiting period became prolonged, and the husband had intercourse during the waiting period. Because intercourse with a revocably divorced woman is permissible. So by this intercourse, revocation is also established and the child's lineage is also established. And if the child is born within less than two years, then this woman becomes bain (irrevocably divorced) from her husband, and the child's lineage from her husband will be established. She becomes bain because giving birth causes irrevocable divorce. And the reason for establishing lineage is that if the intercourse took place during marriage, it is obvious; and if intercourse took place during the waiting period, lineage is still established because intercourse with a revocably divorced woman is legally permissible. But the husband will not be considered as having revoked by this intercourse. Because if it is possible that the intercourse occurred after divorce, it is also possible that the intercourse occurred before divorce. So revocation becomes doubtful, and due to doubt, revocation is not established. For this reason, in this case, revocation will not be established. And if the child is born more than two years from the time of divorce, then revocation is undoubtedly established. Because in this case, the seed definitely occurred after divorce. Since the maximum duration of pregnancy is two years and the apparent situation is that this seed is from that person, because fornication from the woman is negated. So when intercourse is done with the revocably divorced woman during the waiting period, then this person will be considered as having revoked by that intercourse.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Hidayah commentary on establishing lineage (nasab) in cases of revocable divorce (talaq raj'i). The author first states the general rule: a child born to a revocably divorced woman is attributed to the husband if the child is born within the waiting period or after it, with certain conditions. The key distinction is the time of birth relative to the divorce. If the child is born two years or more after the divorce, revocation (ruju') is established because the seed must have occurred after the divorce (since maximum pregnancy is two years) and the woman is presumed free from fornication. If the child is born within two years, the woman becomes bain (irrevocably divorced) due to giving birth, but lineage is still established because the seed could have been from before the divorce or during the waiting period (which is permissible). However, in the latter case, the husband is not considered to have revoked because of doubt about when the intercourse occurred. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of handling probability and certainty in family law: lineage is established on the basis of possibility (ihtimal) and precaution (ihtiyat), while revocation requires certainty (yaqin). The proof is rational: based on the maximum pregnancy period of two years (a Hanafi position) and the legal permissibility of intercourse during the 'iddah of revocable divorce.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity; the legal relationship between father and child.
علوق ('uluq): The seed or conception; the moment when sperm meets ovum.
رجعت (ruj'ah): Revocation of divorce during the 'iddah period; the husband's right to take back his wife without a new contract.
معتدہ رجعیہ (mu'taddah raj'iyyah): A woman in the waiting period of a revocable divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In revocable divorce, a child's lineage is established based on possibility, but revocation requires certainty; timing of birth within or after two years determines the ruling.

Lineage After Irrevocable Divorce: The Two-Year Rule and the Claim Exception
Ruling with rational proof on lineage after irrevocable divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for lineage of a child born to a mabtutah within and after two years, and explain when the husband's claim establishes paternity.

Core Idea
Lineage is established by possibility within two years; after two years, only if the husband claims paternity.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the delicate question of paternity when a woman gives birth after an irrevocable divorce. The Hanafi school balances the precaution (ihtiyat) of preserving lineage with the certainty that the marriage has ended. The key is the two-year maximum pregnancy period and the husband's option to accept paternity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a child born to an irrevocably divorced woman (mabtutah). The ruling: lineage from the ex-husband is established if born within two years, not if born at two years, unless claimed by the husband.
Focus on the two distinct time frames and the exception.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is rational ( dalil 'aqli): the possibility that conception occurred before divorce, as the maximum pregnancy in Hanafi is two years. There is no certainty that the firash ended before conception.
This is based on istishab (presumption of continuity) of the marital bed.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning: since the pregnancy can be from before divorce, we preserve lineage as a precaution (ihtiyat). The legal principle 'al-walad li'l-firash' applies as long as the firash is not proven to have ended.
The key term is ihtimal (possibility), not certainty.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that the child inherits from the ex-husband and carries his name. If the child is born after two years, no inheritance or lineage without claim.
This is a major difference from other schools with shorter maximum pregnancy.
5
Examine the exception: husband's claim
If the husband claims the child even after two years, lineage is established because he voluntarily accepts paternity. The basis is the possibility of intercourse under shubhah during the 'iddah.
This shows the school's emphasis on voluntary acknowledgment and caution towards lineage.

And the irrevocably divorced woman: her child's lineage is established if she gives birth within less than two years, because it is possible that the child existed at the time of divorce, so it is not certain that the marital bed ceased before conception; thus lineage is established as a precaution. And if she gives birth at exactly two years from the time of separation, it is not established, because the pregnancy occurred after divorce, so it is not from him, since intercourse with her is forbidden. Unless he claims it, because he has taken it upon himself. And there is a basis: that he had intercourse with her under a doubt during the waiting period. Translation: And the woman who has been given an irrevocable divorce – the lineage of her child (from the husband) will be established when she gives birth within less than two years. Because there is a possibility that the child existed at the time of divorce. So it is not certain that the marital bed ceased before conception. Therefore, as a precaution, lineage is established. And if that woman gives birth at exactly two years from the time of separation, lineage is not established because the pregnancy occurred after divorce. So it will not be from that man, because intercourse with that woman is forbidden. Except if he claims it, because he has taken the lineage upon himself. And one basis for this is that he had intercourse with her due to a doubt during the waiting period. Explanation: The scenario is that if a woman has been given one irrevocable divorce or three divorces, then within less than two years from the time of separation, a child is born, then the child's lineage will be established from the husband of that irrevocably divorced woman. The proof is that there is a possibility that the child's sperm had settled at the time of divorce. So it is not certain that the proper marital bed had ceased before the sperm settled. Therefore, as a precaution, lineage is established. And if the child is born at exactly two years from the time of separation, lineage is not established because in this case the pregnancy definitely occurred after divorce. Because if the occurrence of pregnancy before divorce is accepted, then the pregnancy period would exceed two years, and that is invalid. So when the pregnancy occurred after divorce, and intercourse with an irrevocably divorced woman is forbidden, then it becomes clear that this child is not from that man's sperm, and when the pregnancy is not from his sperm, then lineage from him is not established. However, if this person claims that this child is from his sperm, then lineage from him will be established, even if the child is born more than two years from the time of separation. The proof is that this person has taken the child's lineage upon himself, and one juristic justification is that this person, during the waiting period, thought it was permissible and had intercourse with this irrevocably divorced woman. And since caution is exercised in establishing lineage, in this case also lineage is established. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning a woman who has been given an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in or three divorces). The key principle is that lineage from the former husband is established if the child is born within two years from the date of separation (divorce). The reason is the possibility that conception occurred before the divorce, even if the woman's 'iddah ended before birth. Since the maximum pregnancy period according to Hanafis is two years, if birth occurs within two years, it is possible the child was conceived before the divorce, so lineage is affirmed as a precaution. If birth occurs exactly two years or more after separation, it is certain that conception occurred after divorce, and since intercourse with an irrevocably divorced woman is forbidden, the child cannot be attributed to the ex-husband. However, an exception is made if the ex-husband claims the child: he can voluntarily accept paternity, and then lineage is established. The juristic basis for this exception is the possibility that the man had intercourse with her during her 'iddah under the mistaken belief that it was permissible (e.g., if he thought the 'iddah had not ended), which is a form of intercourse under shubhah (doubt). The Hanafi school gives weight to cautious preservation of lineage (ihtiyat) where possible.

Key Terms
مبتوتة (mabtutah): A woman who has been given an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in or three divorces), after which the husband cannot take her back except with a new marriage contract.
فراش (firash): The marital bed or legal matrimonial bond; the basis for attributing paternity to the husband. The rule 'al-walad li'l-firash' applies.
شبهہ (shubhah): Legal doubt or mistaken belief that an act is permissible; here, the husband may have intercourse thinking the 'iddah is still ongoing, which is a valid basis for establishing lineage if he claims the child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an irrevocably divorced woman gives birth exactly two years after the divorce, when is the child's lineage established?
A) Always, because of the two-year maximum pregnancy.
B) Never, because the pregnancy must have occurred after divorce.
C) Only if the husband claims the child.
D) Only if the woman did not remarry.

Key Takeaway
Lineage from an irrevocable divorce is established by possibility within the two-year Hanafi maximum pregnancy, and by the husband's claim thereafter.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Lineage for Minor Woman in Irrevocable Divorce
Intra-Hanafi dispute on lineage for minor woman after irrevocable divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf) on establishing lineage when a minor woman gives birth after irrevocable divorce, and explain the legal reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
A minor's 'iddah ends by months with certainty; a child born nine months later cannot be from the ex-husband—unless you accept possibility of intercourse during 'iddah.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding paternity of a child born to a minor woman (saghirah) after an irrevocable divorce. The key lies in how the 'iddah of a minor who does not menstruate is determined: by the passage of three months. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani argue that once those three months pass, the 'iddah ends definitively, so any child born at nine months must have been conceived after the 'iddah, thus not from the ex-husband. Abu Yusuf, however, maintains that since the woman is still within the 'iddah period and has not acknowledged its end, it is possible she became pregnant during the 'iddah, so lineage can be established up to two years.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A minor woman (saghirah) capable of intercourse is given an irrevocable divorce. She gives birth at nine months from the date of divorce. The question is whether the child is attributed to the ex-husband.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: Lineage is not established unless birth occurs within less than nine months. Abu Yusuf: Lineage is established up to two years.
3
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa & Muhammad: The minor's 'iddah ends by passage of three months (Quran 65:4). This is a legal certainty that does not admit disagreement. After 'iddah, intercourse is forbidden (haram). Therefore, a child at nine months cannot be from the ex-husband. Abu Yusuf: The minor is still in 'iddah (she did not acknowledge its end), and it is possible she had intercourse during the 'iddah (perhaps due to shubhah). Therefore, lineage can be established within the maximum pregnancy period of two years.
Focus on the legal certainty of the 'iddah's end vs. the possibility of continued marital relations.
4
Identify the key point of disagreement
The nature of the 'iddah's conclusion: Is it an objective, legal determination (passage of time) that gives certainty, or can it be overridden by the woman's lack of acknowledgment and the possibility of pregnancy?
This is the core usuli difference underlying the ruling.
5
Determine practical consequences
Under the majority view (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad), if the child is born at nine months, the ex-husband has no obligation; the child's lineage is not established. Under Abu Yusuf, the ex-husband is the legal father, affecting inheritance, maintenance, and mahram relationships.
Also note the extension to revocable divorce: Abu Yusuf extends the period to 27 months (three months 'iddah + two years pregnancy).

Source Text

فان كانت المبتوتة صغيرة يجامع مثلها فجائت بولد لتسعة اشهر لم يلزمه حتى تاتى به لاقل من تسعة اشهر عندابي حنيفة و محمد و قال ابويوسف يثبت النسب منه الى سنتين لانها معتدة يحتمل ان تكون حاملا ولم تقربا نقضاء العدة فاشبهت الكبيرة ولهما ان لانقضاء عدتها جهة معينة وهو الاشهر فبمضيها يحكم الشرع بالانقضاء وهو فى الدلالة فوق اقرارها لانه لا يحتمل الخلاف والاقرار يحتمله وان كانت مطلقة طلاق رجعيا فكذالك الجواب عندهما وعنده يثبت الى سبعة وعشرين شهرا لانه يجعل و اطیافی اخر العدة و هى الثلثة الاشهر ثم تاتى به لاكثر مدة الحمل وهو سنتان وان كانت الصغيرة ادعت الحبل في العدة فالجواب فيها وفي الكبيرة سواء لان باقرارها يحكم ببلوغها

If the irrevocably divorced woman is a minor with whom intercourse is possible, and she gives birth at nine months, it is not binding on him until she gives birth within less than nine months according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: Lineage is established from him up to two years, because she is in the waiting period, it is possible she is pregnant, and she did not acknowledge the end of the waiting period, so she is like an adult woman. Their proof (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the end of her 'iddah has a specific method, which is months. With the passage of months, the law rules that the 'iddah has ended, and this is stronger in indication than her own acknowledgment, because it does not admit of disagreement, while her acknowledgment does. And if she was divorced with a revocable divorce, then the same answer applies according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and according to him (Abu Yusuf?), it is established up to twenty-seven months, because he places intercourse at the end of the 'iddah, which is three months, and then she gives birth at the maximum duration of pregnancy, which is two years. And if the minor woman claims pregnancy during the 'iddah, the answer for her and for an adult woman is the same, because by her acknowledgment it is ruled that she has reached puberty. Translation: So if the irrevocably divorced woman is a minor with whom intercourse is possible, then she gives birth at nine months (from the time of divorce), it is not binding on him until she gives birth within less than nine months, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: Lineage is established from him up to two years, because she is in the waiting period, it is possible she is pregnant, and she did not acknowledge the end of the waiting period, so she resembles an adult woman. Their proof (the two) is that the end of her 'iddah has a specific means, which is months. With their passing, the law rules the 'iddah has ended, and that is stronger in indication than her own acknowledgment, because it does not admit of disagreement, while her acknowledgment does. And if she was divorced with a revocable divorce, then the same answer applies according to them, and according to him (Abu Hanifa?) it is established up to twenty-seven months, because he places intercourse at the end of the 'iddah, which is three months, and then she gives birth at the maximum duration of pregnancy, which is two years. And if the minor woman claims pregnancy during the 'iddah, the answer for her and for an adult woman is the same, because by her acknowledgment it is ruled that she has reached puberty.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Abu Hanifa, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Abu Yusuf regarding the lineage of a child born to a minor woman (saghirah) who has been given an irrevocable divorce. The context: a minor girl who is of such an age that intercourse is possible (i.e., she has reached the age where pregnancy can occur) is divorced irrevocably. She gives birth at nine months from the date of divorce. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say: lineage is not established unless she gives birth within less than nine months. Their reasoning: the 'iddah of a minor woman (who has not menstruated) is three months (by Quranic rule). Once three months pass, the 'iddah ends by law with certainty. Since the child is born at nine months, it could only have been conceived after the 'iddah, and intercourse after 'iddah with an irrevocably divorced woman is forbidden. Abu Yusuf, however, argues: lineage is established up to two years from the divorce, because she is in the 'iddah (she did not acknowledge its end), and it is possible she is pregnant from intercourse during the 'iddah (which is permissible in revocable divorce but not in irrevocable? Actually the text says she resembles an adult woman where lineage is established within two years). Abu Yusuf's position is based on the possibility that the 'iddah did not actually end (the minor may not know or acknowledge it), and therefore intercourse could have occurred under the belief it was still the 'iddah. The text then mentions a scenario of revocable divorce: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the same rule applies (lineage not established at nine months? Wait: 'fakadhalik al-jawab 'indahuma' – the same answer applies according to them, meaning that even for revocable divorce, child at nine months is not attributed? But earlier for revocable divorce with an adult, lineage was established; for a minor, perhaps different. Then it says 'wa 'indahu yathbutu ila sab'a wa 'ishrina shahran' – according to him (Abu Hanifa?) it is established up to twenty-seven months, because he places intercourse at the end of the 'iddah (three months) and then she gives birth at the maximum of two years. There is some confusion in the text; the pronoun references are ambiguous. The standard Hanafi position for a minor with revocable divorce is that if she gives birth within less than nine months, lineage is not established? Actually the text seems to say: for revocable divorce, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the same (i.e., not established at nine months, only if less than nine months), and according to Abu Yusuf, it is established up to twenty-seven months. This is a technical intra-madhhab difference that the student should note. Finally, if the minor woman herself claims to be pregnant during the 'iddah, then her claim is accepted (and she is deemed to have reached puberty), and the ruling is the same as for an adult woman.

Key Terms
صغیرہ (saghirah): A minor girl who has not reached puberty but is of an age where intercourse is possible (usually around nine years old).
مدت حمل (muddat al-haml): The maximum duration of pregnancy, which Hanafis hold as two years.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) less than 9 months
C) 2 years
D) 27 months

Key Takeaway
For a minor woman in irrevocable divorce, the 'iddah ends by passage of three months with certainty; childbirth nine months later conclusively falls outside the 'iddah, so lineage is not established, per the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).

intermediate

Lineage of a Child Born to a Divorced Minor Girl
Intra-Hanafi dispute on lineage from a minor divorced girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on lineage establishment for a minor divorced girl, apply the proofs of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad versus Abu Yusuf, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The Shariah's fixed 3-month 'iddah overrides the woman's claim, limiting lineage to 9 months; Abu Yusuf extends to 2/27 months by qiyas.

This passage examines an important intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the lineage of a child born to a minor girl who has been divorced. The ruling affects paternity attribution and has significant practical implications. At the heart of the dispute is the interaction between a fixed Shariah ruling (three-month 'iddah for minors) and the possibility of pregnancy beyond that period. Understanding the reasoning of each imam sharpens your ability to weigh proofs and prioritize Shariah rulings over individual claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and two positions
A minor divorced girl (murahiqah) gives birth. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that lineage is established only if the child is born within 9 months of divorce (for both ba'in and raj'i). Abu Yusuf holds that lineage can be established up to 2 years for ba'in and 27 months for raj'i.
2
Examine Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf analogizes the minor to an adult woman who did not acknowledge the end of 'iddah. Since an adult can have pregnancy up to 2 years, the minor, by analogy, should also have that period. For raj'i, he adds the 3-month 'iddah to the 2-year pregnancy maximum because intercourse is permissible during 'iddah.
His reasoning is based on possibility (ihtimal) and qiyas.
3
Analyse the proof of the two parties
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rely on the Quranic verse (65:4) that fixes the 'iddah for minors as three months. Upon completion, Shariah conclusively rules the 'iddah over, and this ruling is stronger than the woman's acknowledgment because it is definitive (qat'i) and admits no opposite. Thus, any pregnancy after three months cannot be from the ex-husband, except if it began before the 'iddah ended (within 9 months total).
The definitive nature of the Shariah ruling (hukm shar'i) outweighs individual probability.
4
Determine the operative ruling
The text sides with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, giving preference to the conclusive Shariah ruling over speculative possibility. The mufta bihi (relied-upon opinion) in the Hanafi school is the 9-month limit for both types of divorce.
Abu Yusuf's opinion is a valid ikhtilaf but is not adopted in fatwa.

کا نسب لازم نہ ہوگا۔ حتی کہ (اگر) نو ماہ سے کم میں بچہ پیدا ہوا تو ( نسب ثابت ہوگا ) ۔ ( یہ ) امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ہے اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ دو سال تک اس سے نسب ثابت ہوگا۔ ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس معتدہ میں احتمال ہے کہ حاملہ ہو اور اس نے عدت گذر جانے کا اقرار نہیں کیا ہے۔ پس بالغہ عورت کے مشابہ ہوگئی اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس عورت کی عدت گذر جانے کا ایک وقت معین ہے اور وہ عدت کے مہینہ ہیں۔ تو ان کے گذر جانے پر شریعت نے اس کی عدت گذرنے کا حکم دے دیا اور یہ اس عورت کے اقرار سے بڑھ کر ہے۔ کیونکہ حکم شرع خلاف کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا ہے اور اقرار اس کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اور اگر اس صغیرہ کو طلاق رجعی دی گئی ہو، تو طرفین کے نزدیک یہی حکم ہے اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ستائیس ماہ تک نسب ثابت ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عدت کے آخر میں شوہر کو وطی کرنے والا قرار دیا جائے گا اور وہ تین ماہ ہیں۔ پھر یہ عورت اکثر مدت حمل میں بچہ لائی اور وہ دو سال ہیں اور گر صغیرہ نے عدت کے اندر حاملہ ہونے کا دعوی کیا ہو تو اس میں اور کبیرہ میں حکم یکساں ہے۔ کیونکہ صغیرہ کے اقرار جمل سے اس کے بالغہ ہونے کا حکم دے دیا جائے گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر وہ عورت جس کو ایک طلاق بائن یا تین طلاقیں دی گئی ہوں۔ ایسی نابالغہ ہے۔ جس کے ساتھ جماع کیا جا سکتا ہے اور پھر طلاق کے وقت سے نو ماہ پر اس نے بچہ جنا ، اور اس عورت نے عدت گذرنے کا بھی اقرار نہیں کیا ، تو ایسی صورت میں اس کے شوہر کے ذمہ نسب لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ ہاں ! اگر نو ماہ سے کم میں بچہ پیدا ہو گیا تو نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ یہ تفصیل طرفین کے نزدیک ہے اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ طلاق کے وقت سے دو سال تک نسب ثابت ہو گا۔

Chapter of Proof of Lineage. (Lineage) will not be established. Even if (if) the child is born in less than nine months, (then lineage will be established). (This) is according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, and Imam Abu Yusuf said that till two years lineage will be established from him. The proof of Abu Yusuf is that this woman in her waiting period has the possibility of being pregnant and she has not acknowledged the passing of the waiting period. So she becomes similar to an adult woman. And the proof of the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that for this woman there is a fixed time for the passing of the waiting period, and that is the months of the waiting period. So upon their passing, the Shariah has given the ruling of the completion of her waiting period, and this is stronger than the woman's own acknowledgment. Because the ruling of Shariah does not admit of possibility of its opposite, whereas acknowledgment does admit that possibility. And if this minor girl was given a revocable divorce, then according to the two parties the same ruling applies, and according to Abu Yusuf lineage will be established up to twenty-seven months. Because at the end of the waiting period the husband is deemed to have intercourse, and that is three months. Then this woman delivered the child at the maximum duration of pregnancy, and that is two years. And if the minor girl claimed pregnancy during the waiting period, then the ruling is the same for her and for an adult woman. Because due to the minor's acknowledgment, she will be deemed to have become adult. Explanation: This issue is that if a woman who was given a single irrevocable divorce or triple divorce is a minor with whom intercourse is possible, and then she gives birth at nine months from the time of divorce, and she has not acknowledged the passing of the waiting period, then in such a case the husband is not obligated with the lineage. Yes! If the child is born in less than nine months, then lineage will be established. This detail is according to the two parties, and Imam Abu Yusuf said that from the time of divorce, lineage will be established up to two years. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that our discourse is about a minor who has been cohabited (madkhul biha), and a minor so cohabited has the possibility of pregnancy, and regarding the time of pregnancy there are two possibilities. One is that she was pregnant at the time of divorce, then in that case her waiting period ends with delivery and lineage is established. The second possibility is that she became pregnant after the completion of three months of waiting period. So this minor becomes similar to an adult woman. Because she did not acknowledge the passing of the waiting period. Therefore, like an adult, her child's lineage will be up to two years. And the proof of the two parties is that for this woman, there is a fixed time for the completion of her waiting period known to all, and that is three months of waiting period. Allah the Exalted says: 'Wallā'ī lam yaḥiḍna...' meaning those women who do not menstruate, their waiting period is three months. So upon the passing of these three months, the Shariah will give the ruling of the completion of her waiting period, whether this woman acknowledges the passing of the waiting period or not, and regarding indicating the completion of the waiting period, the ruling of the Shariah is stronger than the woman's acknowledgment. Because the ruling of Shariah does not admit the possibility of its opposite, whereas the woman's acknowledgment admits the possibility of being contrary and false. So if the woman acknowledged the passing of the waiting period and then gave birth after six months, lineage would not be established. So it is established that if a minor girl gave birth at nine months from the time of divorce, the lineage of this child will not be established. And if that minor was given a revocable divorce, then according to the two parties the same ruling applies, i.e., if the child is born in less than nine months from the time of divorce, lineage is established; otherwise not. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf, lineage will be established up to twenty-seven months. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that since intercourse with a revocably divorced woman during the waiting period is permissible, therefore it is possible that he had intercourse at the end of the waiting period, and then the child was born at the maximum duration of pregnancy. In this way it will be twenty-seven months: three months of waiting period and two years (the maximum duration of pregnancy). Thus, if the child is born at twenty-seven months from the time of divorce, his lineage will be established. And if the minor girl claimed her pregnancy during the waiting period, then the ruling is the same for both adult and minor. Because due to her acknowledgment of pregnancy, she will be deemed adult, since she is more aware of her waiting period. Therefore, in the case of irrevocable divorce, if the child is born in less than two years, lineage is established; and in the case of revocable divorce, if the child is born in less than twenty-seven months, lineage is established.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the establishment of lineage for a child born to a divorced minor girl who has reached the age where intercourse is possible but has not yet menstruated. The key issue is the maximum period after divorce within which a child's lineage can be attributed to the ex-husband. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (the two parties, 'tarfayn') hold that if the child is born within nine full months from the time of divorce, lineage is established; if born after nine months, it is not. Their proof is based on the Quranic verse (Surah at-Talaq, 65:4) which fixes the 'iddah for minor girls (who do not menstruate) as three months. Upon completion of those three months, the Shariah definitively considers the 'iddah ended, regardless of the woman's own acknowledgment. Since the Shariah's ruling is conclusive and not subject to contrary probability, while a woman's acknowledgment may be false, the expiration of the three months is a stronger indicator than her claim. Therefore, if she delivers after nine months (three months 'iddah plus six months minimum pregnancy), the child cannot be attributed to the ex-husband because the 'iddah had ended and any subsequent pregnancy could be from another man. Only if the child is born before nine months (i.e., within the three-month 'iddah) is the lineage certain, as conception must have occurred during the marriage. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees and extends the period to two years for an irrevocable divorce and twenty-seven months for a revocable divorce. His reasoning is based on possibility: a minor cohabited woman can be pregnant, and she may not have acknowledged the completion of 'iddah. By analogy (qiyas) with an adult woman, he allows lineage up to two years (maximum duration of pregnancy) from the divorce for a ba'in divorce. For a revocable divorce, he adds the three-month 'iddah to the two-year pregnancy period, totaling twenty-seven months, because intercourse is permissible during the 'iddah and could have occurred at its end. The passage also notes that if the minor girl herself claims pregnancy during the 'iddah, then the ruling aligns with that of an adult woman (kabirah), because her acknowledgment is given weight as she is more aware of her condition. The passage provides a detailed exposition of the proofs on both sides, with Imam Abu Yusuf emphasizing probability and the two parties emphasizing the definitive ruling of Shariah.

Key Terms
مراقبه (murahiqah): A minor girl nearing puberty, who has not yet menstruated but is of an age where intercourse is possible (usually between 9 and 12 years).
عدت گذرنے کا اقرار (iddat guzarnay ka iqrar): The woman's verbal acknowledgment that her 'iddah period has expired.
طلاق رجعی (talaq raj'i): A revocable divorce where the husband can take the wife back during the 'iddah without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 9 months
B) 2 years
C) 27 months
D) 6 months

Key Takeaway
For a minor divorced girl, the Shariah's fixed 'iddah (3 months) is conclusive, establishing lineage only if the child is born within 9 months; Abu Yusuf's extended periods are based on probability and are not the relied-upon position.

Lineage of Child Born to Widow Within Two Years: Hanafi Majority vs. Imam Zufar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on paternity within two years

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority ruling on paternity for a child born to a widow within two years, explain Imam Zufar's objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the concept of 'iddah completion by delivery.

Core Idea
A child born to a widow within two years of death is the deceased's heir, even if monthly 'iddah has ended, because delivery also completes 'iddah.

This passage from the chapter on establishing lineage addresses a critical question: when a widow gives birth after her four-month-ten-day 'iddah has elapsed, is the child's paternity still attributed to the deceased husband? The majority of the Hanafi school say yes, within two years. But Imam Zufar dissents, arguing that once the monthly 'iddah ends, the Sharī‘ah has determined the end of the waiting period, so any later child cannot be from the deceased. Understanding this dispute requires careful analysis of the nature of 'iddah and the role of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi ruling
Identify the ruling as stated in the text: lineage is established for a child born up to two years after the husband's death. This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
The two-year period is based on the maximum duration of pregnancy in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Identify Imam Zufar's objection and his dalil
Zufar argues that if birth occurs six months after the monthly 'iddah (4 months 10 days) ends, lineage is not established. His evidence: once the monthly 'iddah expires, the Shar‘ has ruled that the 'iddah is complete; any later birth must be from another man. He draws an analogy (qiyas) with a minor girl whose 'iddah ends by months and who cannot be pregnant.
Zufar's qiyas relies on the idea that the monthly 'iddah is the sole determinant of the end of the waiting period.
3
Analyze the majority's response (naqd al-qiyas)
The majority respond that Zufar's analogy with a minor girl is invalid because an adult woman is capable of pregnancy – delivery (wad‘ al-haml) is an independent way to complete 'iddah. For a minor, the default (aṣl) is non-pregnancy, so only monthly 'iddah applies. For an adult, both monthly completion and delivery are recognized.
The key distinction: the 'iddah of an adult woman can end by either months or delivery; the 'iddah of a minor can only end by months.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If Zufar's view were followed, the child would have no paternal lineage, losing inheritance and family ties. Under the majority, the child is fully attributed to the deceased husband.
This affects inheritance, guardianship, and maintenance.
5
Note the mufta bihi position
The majority position is accepted for fatwa. Ashraf al-Hidayah rejects Zufar's qiyas and upholds the two-year rule.
Later Hanafi works (e.g., Radd al-Muhtār) confirm the majority view.

صغیرہ پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
Chapter on Establishing Lineage. The lineage of a child born to a woman whose husband died is established between the death and two years. Zufar said: If she gives birth after the completion of the 'iddah of death by six months, lineage is not established because the law has ruled the completion of her 'iddah by months to determine the manner, so it becomes as if she acknowledged the completion, as we explained in the case of a minor. But we say: Her 'iddah has another manner of completion, which is delivery of the child, unlike the minor because the default for her is non-pregnancy, as she is not a vessel before puberty, and there is doubt. (Urdu translation and commentary follows explaining the ruling and the dispute with Zufar, concluding that analogy with a minor girl is incorrect.)
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Zufar and the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) regarding the paternity of a child born to a widow. The ruling from the majority is that if a widow gives birth within two years of her husband's death, the child's lineage is established to the deceased husband. Imam Zufar argues that if she gives birth six months after completing the 'iddah of death (4 months 10 days), lineage is not established because the 'iddah had already ended by months, analogous to a minor girl whose 'iddah ends by months without possibility of pregnancy. The majority responds that for an adult woman, delivery is also a means of completing 'iddah; unlike a minor who is incapable of pregnancy before puberty. Thus, the default for the minor is non-pregnancy, but for an adult, pregnancy is possible even after the monthly 'iddah period. Therefore, the analogy with a minor is invalid, and the child's lineage is established if born within two years, even if after the monthly 'iddah.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity; the legal relationship between a father and child.
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarrying; for death it is 4 months 10 days, or until delivery if pregnant.
صغيرة (saghīrah): Minor girl who has not yet reached puberty; she is not considered capable of pregnancy.

Key Takeaway
A child born to a widow within two years of her husband's death is legally attributed to him, as the 'iddah can be terminated by delivery regardless of monthly completion.

Paternity When a Woman in 'Iddah Acknowledges End and Gives Birth
Ruling on paternity when a woman in 'iddah acknowledges its end then gives birth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paternity when a woman in 'iddah acknowledges the end of her 'iddah and then gives birth, and explain the proof based on the minimum pregnancy period.

Core Idea
Certainty (yaqin) overrides doubt (shakk): a birth within less than six months exposes the lie in her acknowledgment.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we examine a nuanced case: a woman in 'iddah claims her waiting period has ended, then gives birth. The question is whether the child's lineage is attributed to her former husband. The answer turns on the timing of the birth relative to her acknowledgment. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi commitment to epistemological certainty (yaqin) in legal proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its two scenarios
The act is a woman in 'iddah acknowledging the end of her 'iddah, then giving birth. Two possibilities: birth in less than six months, or birth at six months or more.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text uses reasoning based on the minimum pregnancy period (six months) and the principle that certainty overrides doubt.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
If birth <6 months, she must have been pregnant at the time of acknowledgment, so her claim is false (yaqin). Paternity is established. If birth ≥6 months, there is possibility of conception after acknowledgment (shakk), so paternity is not established.
4
Note the scope
The ruling applies to all types of 'iddah: revocable divorce, irrevocable divorce, and widowhood.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab status
While the Hanafi position is as stated, other schools may have a different minimum pregnancy period or different weight on acknowledgment, but the Hanafi view is settled within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و اذا اعترفت المعتدة بانقضاء عدتها ثم جاءت بالولد لاقل من ستة اشهر يثبت نسبه لانه ظهر كذبها بيقين فبطل الاقراروان جاءت به لستة اشهر لم يثبت لا نالم نعلم ببطلان الاقرار لاحتمال الحدوث بعده وهذا اللفظ باطلاق يتناول كل معتدة
ترجمہ اور جب معدہ نے اپنی عدت گذرنے کا اقرار کیا پھر اس نے ( اقرار کے وقت سے ) چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ جنا تو اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ معتدہ کا جھوٹا ہونا یقین کے ساتھ معلوم ہو گیا۔ اس وجہ سے اس کا اقرار باطل ہو گیا اور اگر اس نے چھ ماہ میں بچہ جنا تو نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اقرار کے باطل ہونے کا ہمیں علم نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اقرار کے بعد حمل پیدا ہونے کا احتمال ہے اور یہ لفظ اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے ہر معدہ کو شامل ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ معتدہ نے کہا کہ میری عدت گزرگئی۔ پھر اس کے اقرار کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم مدت میں بچہ ہو گیا تو اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب اقرار کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم مدت میں بچہ پیدا ہو گیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ اقرار کے وقت یہ معدہ حاملہ تھی اور چونکہ حاملہ کی عدت وضع حمل ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے یہ معتدہ انقضاء عدت کا اقرار کرنے میں جھوٹی ہوگی اور جب اقرار میں جھوٹی قرار پائی تو اقرار ہی باطل ہو گیا اور جب عدت گزرنے کے بارے میں اقرار باطل ہو گیا تو بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا اور اگر اقرار کے وقت سے پورے چھ ماہ میں بچہ پیدا ہوا تو نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں یہ احتمال ہے کہ اقرار کے بعد حمل پیدا ہوا ہو۔ اس وجہ سے بطلان اقرار کا یقین نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مائن کا قول اذا اعترفت المعتدہ اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے ہر معتدہ کو شامل ہے۔ خواہ معتدہ رجعیہ ہو یا معتدہ بائنہ اور یا معتدہ وفات سب کا حکم یہی ہے جو اوپر بیان کیا گیا۔
When a woman in 'iddah acknowledges the completion of her 'iddah, then gives birth to a child in less than six months, his lineage is established because her lie becomes certain, so the acknowledgment is void. If she gives birth at six months, it is not established because we do not know the invalidity of the acknowledgment due to the possibility of conception after it. This word, by its generality, includes every woman in 'iddah. (Urdu translation and commentary follow, explaining the reasoning and that the ruling applies to all types of 'iddah: revocable, irrevocable, and widowhood.)
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof: If a woman in 'iddah claims her 'iddah has ended, but then gives birth within less than six months from that claim, her claim is proven false, and the child's paternity is established to the former husband. This is because a minimum pregnancy period is six months; thus, conception must have occurred before the claim, meaning she was still in 'iddah at that time. If she gives birth exactly six months later, there is a possibility she conceived after the claim, so the claim may be true, and paternity is not established. The ruling applies to all types of 'iddah (divorce revocable, irrevocable, and death). The proof is based on the principle of certainty over doubt.

Key Terms
معتدة (mu'taddah): A woman who is observing 'iddah after divorce or death of husband.
اقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment or admission; here, the woman's statement that her 'iddah has ended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman in 'iddah says her 'iddah has ended, then gives birth exactly six months later. Is the child's paternity established?
A) Yes, because regardless of timing, the birth disproves her claim.
B) No, because there is a possibility she conceived after the claim.
C) Yes, because six months is the minimum pregnancy period.
D) No, because a woman's word is not accepted against her children.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the minimum pregnancy period of six months is used as a criterion to determine whether a woman's acknowledgment of 'iddah completion is truthful; if birth occurs within less than six months, her lie is certain and paternity is established; if at six months or more, doubt remains.

Witness Requirements for Paternity from Woman in ʿIddah
Dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on witness numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the number of witnesses needed to establish paternity from a woman in ʿiddah, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
One woman's testimony suffices to establish paternity from an ʿiddah woman — the marital bed persists.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the evidentiary requirements for establishing the paternity of a child born to a woman in ʿiddah. Abu Hanifa requires two men or a man and two women, while his students Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept the testimony of a single woman. Understanding the reasoning behind each position clarifies the Hanafi concept of firāsh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize the scenario: a woman in ʿiddah gives birth, and the paternity of the child needs to be established. The dispute centers on how many witnesses are required.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa requires two male witnesses or one man and two women to testify to the birth, unless the pregnancy was visible or the husband acknowledged it before birth (in which case no witnesses are needed).
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say that one woman's testimony (the mother's or a midwife) suffices in all cases, because the marital bed (firāsh) continues during ʿiddah.
4
Analyze the reasoning and thamarah al-khilaf
The Sahibayn rely on the persistence of firāsh to establish lineage, requiring only identification of the child. Abu Hanifa argues that ʿiddah ends with the mother's acknowledgment of delivery, so lineage must be proven anew with full testimony. The practical consequence: under the mufta bihi (Sahibayn), a single woman's testimony suffices; under Abu Hanifa, without two witnesses or the exceptions, paternity may not be established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا ولدت المعتدة ولدالم يثبت نسبه عنه ابي حنيفة الا ان يشهد بولا دتها رجلان اورجل وامرأتان الا ان يكون هناك حبل ظاهر او اعتراف من قبل الزوج فيثبت النسب من غير شهادة وقال ابو يوسف و محمد يثبت فى الجميع بشهادة امرأة واحدة لان الفراش قائم بقيام العدة وهو ملزم للنسب والحاجة الى تعيين الولدانه منها فيتعين بشهادتها كمافي حال قيام النكاج ولابي حنيفة ان العدة تنقضي باقرارها بوضع الحمل والمنقضى ليس بحجة فمست الحاجة الى اثبات النسب ابتداء فيشترط كمال الحجة بخلاف ما اذا كان ظهر الحبل اوصدر الاعتراف من الزوج لان النسب ثابت قبل الولادة والتعين يثبت بشهادتها
When a woman in 'iddah gives birth to a child, his lineage is not established according to Abu Hanifa unless two men or one man and two women witness her giving birth, unless there is a visible pregnancy or acknowledgment from the husband, in which case lineage is established without testimony. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is established in all cases by the testimony of one woman because the marital bed (firāsh) remains by the existence of 'iddah, and it necessitates lineage, and there is need to identify the child as hers, so it is identified by her testimony as in the case of a valid marriage. For Abu Hanifa, the 'iddah ends by her acknowledgment of delivery, and what has ended is not a proof, so the need arises to establish lineage anew, thus complete proof is required, unlike when the pregnancy was apparent or the husband acknowledged, because lineage was established before birth and identification is established by her testimony.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the evidentiary requirements to establish paternity when a woman in 'iddah gives birth. Abu Hanifa requires standard testimony of two men or one man and two women, unless there is visible pregnancy or the husband acknowledges, then no witnesses are needed. The Sahibayn argue that one woman's testimony suffices in all cases because the marital bed (firāsh) persists during 'iddah, and the bed necessitates lineage; the only need is to identify the child as hers, which her testimony can do, like during marriage. Abu Hanifa responds that the 'iddah ends (for purposes of firāsh) when the woman acknowledges delivery; what has ended cannot serve as proof, so establishing lineage requires a complete proof (shahāda). The exception is when pregnancy was apparent or the husband acknowledged before birth, because then lineage was already established. The mufta bihi position is the Sahibayn's view, as it is more practical and aligns with the principle of firāsh.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony in court; here, the number of witnesses required.
فراش (firāsh): The marital bed; a legal principle that a child born to a married woman (or a woman in ʿiddah) is attributed to the husband unless proven otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Two men or one man and two women
B) One woman
C) Two women
D) No witnesses are ever required

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's view that one woman's testimony suffices to establish paternity from an iddah woman is the operative Hanafi position, based on the continuity of the marital bed.

Divorce Conditional on Childbirth: Single Woman's Testimony Debate
Intra-Hanafi dispute on women's testimony for ta'liq divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on accepting a single woman's testimony for a conditional divorce, and apply the concept of hujja tamma to distinguish between establishing the birth and the divorce.

Core Idea
A single woman's testimony suffices for the fact of birth but not for the legal consequence (divorce) — the latter requires complete proof.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on a conditional divorce. A husband says to his wife, 'If you give birth, you are divorced.' A midwife testifies that the birth occurred, but the husband denies it. Does the divorce take effect? Abu Hanifa says no, the Sahibayn say yes. The disagreement hinges on the scope of women's testimony: is it limited to the physical fact of birth, or does it extend to the legal derivatives?

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
Read the conditional divorce statement: 'If you give birth, you are divorced.' The condition is birth, the consequence is divorce. A single woman (midwife) testifies to the birth; the husband denies. Identify the key legal question: does her testimony prove the hanth (occurrence of condition)?
The wife's pregnancy may not have been apparent; the husband may have no knowledge.
2
State the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa holds that the divorce does not occur. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that it does occur. Write each position clearly.
This is an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf; both are within the madhhab.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn cite the hadith: 'The testimony of women is permissible in matters that men cannot see.' They argue that since the birth is proven by her testimony, the divorce contingent on it should also be proven. Identify the dalil and its logical structure.
They treat the birth and divorce as inseparable in proof.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa distinguishes: the claim of hanth is a separate legal claim requiring complete proof (hujja tamma: two male witnesses or one male and two females). Women's testimony is accepted for birth only out of necessity (darura) for lineage and other unavoidable matters, but this necessity does not extend to the derivative divorce because divorce can be separated from birth (yanfakku 'anha).
Hujja tamma means full evidentiary proof; a single woman is insufficient for claims beyond necessity.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to Abu Hanifa, the wife is not divorced (though the child's lineage is established). According to the Sahibayn, the wife becomes divorced. Explain how this difference affects the legal status of the wife and the marriage.
The later Hanafi position (mufta bihi) often follows Abu Hanifa due to ihtiyat (caution) in talaq.

And if he said to his wife, 'If you give birth to a child, you are divorced,' then a woman testified to the birth: according to Abu Hanifa, she is not divorced, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said she is divorced, because her testimony is proof in this matter. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The testimony of women is permissible in matters that men cannot see.' And because her testimony is accepted in establishing birth, it is also accepted in what is built upon it, i.e., divorce. Abu Hanifa's proof: she claimed the occurrence of the condition (hanth); thus it is not established except by complete proof (hujja tamma). This is because the testimony of women is allowed out of necessity (darura) regarding birth, so its effect does not appear regarding divorce, since divorce can be separated from birth.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a conditional divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) based on childbirth. The scenario: a man says to his wife, 'If you give birth to a child, you are divorced.' A midwife (single woman) testifies that the child was born, but the husband denies the birth. Abu Hanifa holds that the divorce does not occur, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it does. The Sahibayn argue that a woman's testimony is accepted in matters men cannot normally observe (like childbirth), based on the hadith, and since it is accepted for establishing the birth, it should also be accepted for the divorce that is contingent upon it. Abu Hanifa counters that the woman (wife) is claiming that the condition (hanth) has occurred (i.e., the birth that triggers divorce), and such a claim requires complete proof (hujja tamma). Women's testimony in matters of birth is permitted out of necessity (darura) for establishing lineage and other essential matters, but this necessity does not extend to the divorce itself, which is a separate legal effect that can be independent (yanfakku 'anha). Therefore, the divorce is not proven by the single woman's testimony. The commentary adds that the child's lineage is established (since that is necessary), but the divorce is not.

Key Terms
تعلیق طلاق (ta'liq al-talaq): Conditional divorce: a statement making divorce contingent on a future event.
حنث (hanth): The occurrence of the condition (the contingency) in a conditional statement.
حجت تامہ (hujja tamma): Complete proof: full legal evidence, such as two male witnesses or one male and two females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a man says to his wife 'If you give birth, you are divorced' and a midwife testifies to the birth, why does Abu Hanifa deny the divorce?
A) Because the husband did not witness the birth.
B) Because the midwife's testimony is rejected in all cases.
C) Because the claim of hanth requires complete proof, and a single woman's testimony is insufficient for the legal consequence (divorce), being only a necessity for the physical birth.
D) Because the wife did not confirm the birth herself.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a single woman's testimony can prove childbirth for lineage purposes, but not the occurrence of a conditional divorce; the distinction rests on the scope of necessity (darura) and the requirement of complete proof (hujja tamma) for legal consequences.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Single Woman's Testimony for Conditional Divorce
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony extent in conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the basis of the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the extension of a single woman's testimony from childbirth to a conditional divorce, and apply the principle 'idha thabata al-shay'u thabata bi-lawazimihi' to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Necessity limits proof to its immediate scope; concomitant effects follow establishment.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi disagreement that tests the boundaries of darurah (necessity) in evidence law. When a husband makes divorce conditional on childbirth, and a single midwife testifies to the birth, does the divorce occur? The dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples hinges on whether the exception for women's testimony in childbirth extends to its legal consequences. We will walk through their proofs and the commentator's resolution.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the core legal question
Identify the precise conditional divorce formula and the situation where only one woman testifies to the birth. The question: does that testimony suffice to establish both the birth and the divorce?
Note that the pregnancy was neither apparent nor acknowledged by the husband.
2
Outline Abu Hanifa's position and its reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that the divorce does not occur. Understand his key argument: the wife's claim of breach requires complete proof (hujjat tammah). Women's testimony in childbirth is accepted only by necessity, so it is limited to the birth itself and does not extend to the divorce, which can exist independently.
Abu Hanifa relies on the principle that necessity is measured by its extent (al-darurah tuqaddaru bi-qadariha).
3
Outline the Sahibayn's position and its reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the divorce occurs. Their proof: a hadith (though gharib) that women's testimony is accepted in matters men cannot see; childbirth is such a matter. Since the divorce is conditional on birth, once birth is established, its necessary consequence (the divorce) follows.
They also cite a practice (sunnah) reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah and the principle of lawazim (concomitants).
4
Analyze the commentator's tarjih (preponderance)
The commentator (khadim) critiques Abu Hanifa's argument, stating that although birth and divorce are separable in other contexts, here the divorce is a concomitant of the birth because it is conditional. Applying the rule 'idha thabata al-shay'u thabata bi-lawazimihi', the divorce must be established along with the birth.
Thus, the commentator prefers the Sahibayn's view as stronger. Note that Imam Muhammad's own position on an associated oath requirement remains ambiguous.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa, the woman is not divorced but the child's lineage is established. Under the Sahibayn, the divorce occurs. Understand how this difference affects the status of the marriage and the financial rights of the wife.
This has implications for iddah, mahr, and inheritance.

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا اذا ولدت ولداً فانت طالق پس ایک عورت ( دایہ) نے بچہ پیدا ہونے پر شہادت دی اور شوہر ولادت کا منکر ہے۔ درانحالیکہ اس عورت کا حمل نہ ظاہر تھا اور نہ شوہر نے اس کے حاملہ ہونے کا اقرار کیا تو امام اعظم حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس عورت پر طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ البتہ نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے ایک عورت کی گواہی سے ولادت ثابت ہو جاتی ہے۔ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا عورتوں کی شہادت ہر ایسے امر میں جائز ہے جس کی طرف مردوں کو دیکھنا شرعاً ممنوع ہو۔ پس جب ایک عورت کی شہادت سے ولادت ثابت ہوگئی تو طلاق بھی واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ طلاق ولادت پر معلق کی گئی ہے۔ اس حدیث کے غریب ہونے کی وجہ سے اکثر شراح نے اس کو ذکر نہیں کیا ہے اس کے علاوہ ابن ابی شیبہ نے اپنے مصنف میں ایک روایت بیان کی ہے عن الزهری قال مضت السنة ان يجوز شهادة النساء فيما لا يطلع علیه غیر من فرمایا کہ ان امور میں جن پر عورتوں کے علاوہ کوئی مطلق نہیں ہوسکتا عورتوں کی شہادت کے جواز پر سنت جاری ہے۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب ایک عورت ( دایہ ) کی شہادت ولادت ثابت کرنے میں حجت ہے تو طلاق جو ولادت پر معلق اور مینی ہے اس کو ثابت کرنے میں بھی یقیناً حجت ہوگی۔
اور امام اعظم کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت (بیوی) نے اپنے شوہر پر حانث ہونے کا دعوی کیا یعنی وقوع طلاق کا اور شوہر اس کا منکر ہے۔ الہذا عورت کا یہ دعویٰ بغیر حجت کاملہ کے ثابت نہیں ہوگا اور رہی یہ بات کہ طلاق موقوف ہے ولادت پر اور ولادت ثابت ہو جاتی ہے ایک عورت کی شہادت سے۔ لہذا طلاق جو موقوف ہے اس کا ثبوت بھی ایک عورت کی شہادت سے ہونا چاہئے ۔ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ولادت کے حق میں عورتوں کی شہادت ضرورة معتبر ہے اور جو چیز ضرورۃ ثابت ہو وہ بقدر ضرورت ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی موضع ضرورت سے تجاوز نہیں کرتی ۔ پس ایک عورت کی شہادت سے ولادت ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ ولادت کے وقت مرد موجود نہیں رہتے۔ اسلئے ولادت کے حق میں عورتوں کی شہادت کا ضرورۃ اعتبار کیا گیا ہے۔ البتہ طلاق کے حق میں ایک عورت کی شہادت کا اثر ظاہر نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ طلاق اور ولادت میں کوئی الزام نہیں بلکہ طلاق بغیر ولادت کے اور ولادت بغیر طلاق کے پائی جاتی ہے۔ خادم کا خیال ہے کہ حضرت امام صاحب کی دلیل میں ضعف ہے۔ اس طرح پر کہ بلاشبہ طلاق اور ولادت کے درمیان تلازم نہیں ۔ لیکن اس مسئلہ میں طلاق ولا دت کے لوازم میں سے ہے۔ اسلئے کہ طلاق ولادت پر معلق کی گئی ہے اور معلق باشنی شی ء کے لوازم میں سے ہوتی ہے اور قاعدہ ہے اذا ثبت الشيء ثبت بلوازمہ یعنی جب ٹی ثابت ہوگی تو اپنے تمام لوازم کے ساتھ ثابت ہوگی ۔ لہذا جب ایک عورت کی شہادت سے ولادت ثابت ہو گی تو اس کا لازم یعنی طلاق بھی ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ پس دلیل کی روشنی میں صاحبین کا مسلک راجح معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
And if he said to his wife: 'If you give birth to a child, you are divorced,' and a woman testified to the birth, she is not divorced according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: She is divorced, because her testimony is a proof in that matter. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The testimony of women is permissible in matters that men cannot see.' And because when it is accepted for birth, it is accepted for what is based upon it, i.e., divorce. According to Abu Hanifa: She claimed the breach, so it is not established except by complete proof. And this is because their testimony is necessary concerning birth, so it does not appear concerning divorce, because it can be separated from it. [Then Urdu translation and elaboration follows] ... And the servant (khadim) holds that the Imam's proof is weak, because although there is no necessary connection between birth and divorce, in this case divorce is a consequence of birth, and the rule is: when a thing is established, its consequences are established. So Sahibayn's view is preponderant. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a conditional divorce hinging on childbirth. The scenario: a husband tells his wife, 'If you give birth to a child, you are divorced.' A single woman (midwife) testifies that the wife gave birth, but the husband denies the birth, and the wife's pregnancy was neither apparent nor acknowledged. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the divorce does not occur; only the lineage is established. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that the divorce does occur. Their proof: a hadith (though gharib) that women's testimony is accepted in matters men cannot see, and since childbirth is such a matter, the testimony is accepted for birth and consequently for the dependent divorce. Ibn Abi Shaybah reports a similar practice from al-Zuhri. Abu Hanifa's proof: the wife claims breach of condition (hanath), and her claim requires complete proof (two men or one man and two women). Women's testimony in childbirth is accepted only out of necessity (darurah) and is limited to that necessity; it does not extend to divorce, which can occur independently of birth. The commentator (khadim) critiques Abu Hanifa's argument, citing the principle 'When a thing is established, its concomitants are established' (idha thabata al-shay'u thabata bi-lawazimihi). Since divorce is conditional on birth, once birth is established by the woman's testimony, the divorce follows as a necessary concomitant. Hence, the commentator favors the Sahibayn's view as stronger. The passage also notes that Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir did not explicitly address whether an oath is required from the wife, a matter on which there is disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the two.

Key Terms
حانث (hanith): One who breaks or violates a condition; here, the wife claims the husband is hanith because she gave birth.
حجت تامہ (hujjat tammah): Complete proof sufficient to establish a claim, e.g., testimony of two men or one man and two women.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that allows departure from standard rules, here permitting women's testimony for childbirth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute about a conditional divorce ('if you give birth, you are divorced') with testimony from a single woman, what is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The divorce occurs because women's testimony is accepted in childbirth.
B) The divorce does not occur because the wife's claim requires complete proof; women's testimony is limited to birth by necessity.
C) The divorce occurs only if the husband acknowledges the pregnancy.
D) The divorce occurs only if two women testify.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school is not monolithic on extending darurah from childbirth to its legal consequences; the mufta bihi view (Sahibayn) applies the principle of lawazim to establish the conditional divorce.
